Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are planning a family summer holiday abroad and have shortlisted Paris as your destination. You want to contact a travel agency to get family-friendly package options, pricing, and assistance with bookings and visas.

Options:
a. Write an e-mail to the Manager of the travel agency requesting detailed family holiday packages to Paris, including dates, cost per person, accommodation options, meals, child-friendly activities, and transport arrangements.
b. Write a short phone-call follow-up script to confirm receipt of your e-mail and request an expedited written quote.
c. List all documents and information you should prepare and send to the agency to help them process the booking and support a visa application for your family.
d. Give three key questions you should ask the agency before finalising the booking and explain why each is important.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
To: info@parisfamilytours.com

Subject: Request for Detailed Family Holiday Package to Paris (12–20 August 2025)

Dear Sir/Madam,

I hope you are well. I am planning a family holiday to Paris during our summer break and have heard good things about your agency. We are a family of four (two adults and two children aged 8 and 12) and would like to travel approximately from 12 August 2025 to 20 August 2025 (flexible by ±2 days).

Could you please send me detailed family-friendly package options that include:
- Cost per person and total cost for the family (please specify child rates and any applicable discounts)
- Number of nights and hotel options (3-star, 4-star, and family-suite choices) with meal plans (breakfast only / half-board / full-board)
- Transport arrangements (international flights, airport transfers, local transport or pass options)
- A sample day-by-day itinerary highlighting child-friendly activities (e.g., Disneyland Paris, Louvre family tour, Seine boat cruise, parks and interactive museums)
- Any family-specific amenities (e.g., connecting rooms, kids’ meals, babysitting, child seats in transfers)
- Inclusions and exclusions (entrance fees, local taxes, tipping policy)
- Payment schedule, deposit required, cancellation and refund policy, and travel insurance options
- Visa assistance you provide (document checklist, appointment help, processing time, fees)

Please provide the best available price for the dates above and indicate whether you can hold a provisional booking while I confirm passports and school leave. If you need any further information from me, let me know.

I look forward to your prompt reply.

Thank you.

Sincerely,

[Your Full Name]
[Address]
[Contact number]
[Email]

b
Hello, this is [Your Name]. I sent an e-mail today requesting family holiday packages to Paris for 12–20 August 2025. Could you please confirm you received it? We are a family of four and would appreciate an expedited written quote and a provisional hold on availability for 48 hours while I finalise details. If you need any documents now, I can provide them by e-mail. May I have the name of the staff member handling this and an estimated time for the quote? Thank you very much.

c
Documents and information to prepare and send:
- Scanned valid passports for all family members (bio-data pages)
- Recent passport-size photos (meeting visa specification) for each person
- Completed visa application forms if available / or full names, dates of birth, places of birth as on passports
- Proof of relationship for children (birth certificates; marriage certificate of parents if required)
- Proposed travel dates and full contact details (phone, email, current address)
- Proof of onward/return travel (or request the agency to provide tentative flight reservations)
- Proof of accommodation (agency will provide, but indicate preferred hotel category)
- Travel insurance details or request for agency-provided insurance (names, coverage amounts)
- Proof of funds or bank statements if needed for visa (last 3–6 months) — check embassy requirements
- Employment/student letters / leave letters (for parents and children if required)
- Any special medical information or required vaccinations for family members
- Payment method details for deposit (card, bank transfer) — do not send full card details by insecure e-mail; follow agency’s secure payment process

d
Question 1: What is your cancellation and refund policy (including timelines and any non-refundable charges)?
Reason: Families may need flexibility; knowing deadlines and penalties prevents unexpected costs if plans change.

Question 2: Are child rates age-based and what is the exact age cut-off for discounts or free stays? Are rooms family suites or interconnecting rooms guaranteed?
Reason: Child pricing and room configuration affect both cost and comfort; confirming avoids surprises at check-in and ensures suitable sleeping arrangements.

Question 3: Do you offer visa assistance and what exactly is included (appointment booking, document checking, consulate submission)? What are the typical processing times and additional fees?
Reason: Visa processing can be time-consuming and vary by consulate; understanding what the agency provides helps you plan and avoids last-minute delays.


Explanation:
This solution provides a practical set of deliverables for contacting a travel agency about a family trip. The e-mail (a) is polite, specific about dates, family composition, and requests all necessary package details—this helps the agent produce a tailored quote. The phone script (b) is concise and action-oriented, aimed at confirming receipt and requesting an expedited quote while establishing a contact person and timeline. The document checklist (c) includes standard visa and booking paperwork (passports, photos, proof of relationship, proof of funds, insurance) and advises caution about secure transmission of payment information. The three questions (d) are chosen to cover financial risk (cancellation), practical logistics (child rates and room types), and administrative lead time (visa assistance) — each is explained so you know why the question matters when deciding whether to book. Tone throughout is courteous and businesslike to encourage a helpful response from the agency.

Question:
Suppose your name is Anika/Arif. You study at Greenfield High School in Dhaka. Recently your mother has been transferred to Rangpur for work and your family will relocate there soon. You wish to remain at Greenfield High School and continue your studies there until your SSC examination is over. Prepare the following documents and short writing pieces related to this situation.

Options:
a. Write a formal application to the Headmaster of Greenfield High School requesting a seat in the school hostel until your SSC examination is over.
b. Write a short parental consent form addressed to the hostel warden giving permission for your admission to the hostel and providing emergency contact details.
c. Write a brief notice to your class teacher informing about the change of home address and providing the name and contact of the guardian who will act for you locally.
d. Write a short paragraph (about 50–60 words) explaining why staying in the school hostel will help you prepare better for the SSC examination.

Solution:
a
26 August 2025

To

The Headmaster
Greenfield High School
Dhaka

Subject: Request for allotment of a seat in the school hostel

Dear Sir/Madam,

I am Anika/Arif, a student of Class IX (Roll No. 12) of your esteemed school. My mother has recently been transferred to Rangpur and my family will relocate there shortly. As I wish to continue my studies at Greenfield High School until my SSC examination is completed, I kindly request that you allot me a seat in the school hostel for the required period.

I shall abide by all hostel rules and pay the necessary fees on time. I hope you will kindly consider my application and grant me permission.

Yours obediently,

Anika/Arif
Roll No. 12, Class IX
Contact: 01XXXXXXXXX

b
Parental Consent Form for Hostel Admission

Date: 26 August 2025

To

The Warden
School Hostel
Greenfield High School

I, Mrs./Mr. [Mother's/Father's Name], parent of Anika/Arif (Class IX, Roll No. 12), hereby give my consent for my child to be admitted to the school hostel of Greenfield High School until the completion of the SSC examination. Our family is relocating to Rangpur due to my job transfer.

Name: Mrs./Mr. [Alternate Guardian's Name]
Relation: [Relation]
Phone: 01YYYYYYYY

I authorize the warden and school authorities to take necessary decisions for my child's welfare in my absence.

Signature of Parent/Guardian: __________________
Name: Mrs./Mr. [Mother's/Father's Name]
Contact: 01XXXXXXXXX

c

Date: 26 August 2025

Respected Sir/Madam,

Please be informed that my family will move to Rangpur due to my mother's job transfer. My local guardian for school matters will be Mrs./Mr. [Guardian's Name], contact number 01YYYYYYYY. Thank you for your cooperation.

Yours sincerely,

Anika/Arif
Class IX, Roll No. 12

d
Staying in the school hostel will give me a stable study environment, regular routines, and easy access to teachers and library resources. It will reduce travel time and distractions at home after my family moves. With hostel discipline and peer support, I can concentrate fully on exam preparation and improve my chances of good SSC results.

Explanation:
a) Application to the Headmaster: Use a formal letter format with date, address, subject line, respectful salutation, clear statement of facts (transfer and desire to continue studies), the specific request (seat in hostel), assurance of following rules, and signature with class and roll number. Include a contact number so the school can reach you.

b) Parental consent form: This should explicitly state the parent's permission for hostel admission, mention reason (transfer), and give emergency contact details and an authorized local guardian. A parent's signature is necessary for official acceptance.

c) Notice to class teacher: Short and direct. Inform about change of home address, provide the name and phone number of the local guardian so the teacher and school can contact someone responsible, and request updating records.

d) Short paragraph on benefits: Focus on concrete advantages — stable study environment, routine, proximity to school resources and teachers, reduced travel and distractions, and improved focus for SSC preparation. Keep it within the requested word limit (the provided paragraph is about 56 words).

Tone and formatting guidance: All formal documents should be polite, concise, and include identifying details (name, class, roll number) and contact information. For official requests, mention willingness to follow rules and any practical arrangements (fee payment, guardian details) to reassure the authorities. The parental consent must be signed by the parent/guardian to be valid.

Question #141 (ID: 578723)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You have been asked to prepare materials for a school newsletter about cultivating reading habits among students in the digital era. The newsletter should include a concise composition, tangible benefits, practical habit-building tips, and genre recommendations to appeal to different readers.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition titled "Reading in the Digital Age" suitable for the newsletter.
b. List five clear benefits of regular reading (one sentence each).
c. Suggest three practical ways students can develop a consistent reading habit.
d. Recommend four book genres with a brief reason for each choice.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Reading in the Digital Age

Introduction:
In our rapidly changing world, reading remains a vital skill. Even with screens everywhere, books continue to open minds, fuel imagination, and provide deep knowledge. Digital devices offer convenience, but traditional reading nurtures concentration, critical thinking, and empathy.

Body:
Books—whether physical or electronic—expand vocabulary, improve communication, and develop analytical abilities. Fiction encourages empathy by immersing readers in others’ lives; non-fiction offers facts and frameworks for understanding complex subjects. Regular reading reduces stress, sharpens memory, and supports lifelong learning. For students, reading strengthens academic performance and broadens perspectives beyond curricula.

Challenges and Solutions:
Modern distractions like social media and short-form content fragment attention spans. To counter this, setting aside daily reading time, choosing engaging books, and using reading apps that limit distractions can help. Libraries, book clubs, and family reading routines also foster consistent habits.

Conclusion:
Reading in the digital age requires intention but yields timeless rewards. It cultivates curiosity, empowers decision-making, and connects generations. Whether flipping pages or scrolling screens, making reading a daily practice enriches individual lives and society. Readers who balance digital and print formats gain adaptability, depth of knowledge, and lasting appreciation for stories and ideas across cultures and shared wisdom.

b Five benefits of regular reading:
1. Expands vocabulary and improves written and spoken communication. 
2. Strengthens critical thinking and analytical skills useful across subjects. 
3. Reduces stress and enhances mental focus by providing immersive downtime. 
4. Encourages empathy and social understanding through exposure to diverse perspectives. 
5. Promotes lifelong learning and adaptability in a fast-changing world.

c Three practical ways to build a reading habit:
1. Set a fixed daily reading time (e.g., 20–30 minutes before bed) and treat it as a non-negotiable appointment. 
2. Create a distraction-free reading environment: a comfortable spot, phone on Do Not Disturb, and reachable books or a curated e-reader list. 
3. Use social and goal-based supports: join a book club, track progress with a reading log or app, and celebrate milestones to stay motivated.

d Four recommended book genres with reasons:
1. Fiction (novels/short stories) — builds imagination and empathy through character-driven narratives. 
2. Biography/memoir — offers real-life lessons, inspiration, and historical context. 
3. Popular science/non-fiction — explains complex ideas in accessible ways and sharpens critical thinking. 
4. Fantasy/young adult — highly engaging for reluctant readers and often encourages rapid reading confidence.

Explanation:
The composition (a) was written to be approximately 200 words and structured with clear sections—introduction, body, challenges/solutions, and conclusion—to suit a newsletter audience. The benefits (b) focus on cognitive, emotional, and practical gains that are easy for students and educators to appreciate. The habit-building tips (c) emphasize routine, environment, and social accountability because research and experience show these strategies reliably increase sustained reading. The genre recommendations (d) cover varied tastes and developmental needs: fiction and fantasy for engagement and empathy, biography for real-world learning, and popular science for curiosity and conceptual thinking. Together these parts offer a compact, actionable guide for encouraging reading in a digital context.

Question:
Context: You are asked to write a descriptive composition titled "A Foggy Morning" in 200 words and answer related short tasks below.

Options:
a. Write the 200-word composition titled "A Foggy Morning."
b. Give a five-sentence introduction about a foggy morning.
c. List three effects a foggy morning can have on everyday life.
d. Name two typical foods people enjoy on a foggy morning and describe the general mood it creates.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a A Foggy Morning

Introduction:
A foggy morning arrives like a soft blanket over the earth. The air feels cool and still, and familiar sights become blurred shapes. Streetlights glow like dim moons, and the world seems hushed as if holding its breath. Fog often follows a clear night and forms over fields, rivers, and quiet towns.

Nature’s Appearance:
Trees emerge as shadowy figures while dew clings to spiderwebs and grass. Sounds are muffled; even footsteps seem distant. The sun rises slowly, its light diffused into a pale, golden haze, making everything look dreamy and mysterious.

Effect on Daily Life:
Commuters drive cautiously, headlights cutting thin paths through the mist. Flights and boats sometimes face delays. Farmers appreciate the moisture while photographers and painters find inspiration in the soft tones. Children thrill at playing in the gentle dampness under watchful parents.

Food and Mood:
Warm drinks like tea or hot chocolate feel especially comforting. A foggy morning brings introspection and calm, inviting slow walks and quiet conversation.

Conclusion:
Though it may disrupt schedules, a foggy morning reveals a quieter, softer side of the world, offering moments of peace and wonder. It teaches us to appreciate small beauties in everyday life truly.

(Exact word count: 200 words.)

b A foggy morning drapes the world in a soft, pearly veil. Visibility shrinks and familiar landmarks blend into gentle silhouettes. The air feels cool and carries a subtle dampness that freshens the senses. Sounds are muted, giving the surroundings a tranquil hush. Such mornings invite quiet reflection and slow movement.

c 1) Transport delays and cautious driving: Reduced visibility forces drivers to slow down and can cause delays in road, air, and water travel.
2) Altered outdoor activities: Events, sports, and early-morning chores may be postponed or require extra care.
3) Health and work effects: People with respiratory issues may feel discomfort; deliveries and commutes can be slower, affecting schedules.

d Typical foods: hot tea (or ginger tea) and warm porridge or toast. Mood: calm, introspective, and cozy—people tend to move slowly, enjoy warm drinks, and appreciate quiet moments or gentle company.

Explanation:
This task mirrors the original style: a short descriptive composition plus related sub-tasks. For (a) I produced a cohesive 200-word composition focused on sensory details (sight, sound, touch) and daily effects; I verified the exact word count by counting tokens to reach 200 words. For (b) I distilled the core idea into five concise sentences that set the scene and tone. For (c) I listed practical consequences of fog (transport, activities, health/work) to cover varied impacts. For (d) I chose common comforting foods (hot tea, porridge/toast) and a brief mood description (calm, introspective, cozy) that typically accompany foggy mornings. The composition structure (introduction, nature’s appearance, effects, food and mood, conclusion) follows a familiar school-essay format to make it clear and balanced while maintaining descriptive language and imagery.

Question:
Write a composition on "Memories of Summer Holidays" in 200 words.

Options:
a. Write the 200-word composition on 'Memories of Summer Holidays'.
b. Write a 30-word introduction for the composition.
c. List five sensory-detail phrases (short phrases) drawn from the composition.
d. Write a one-sentence concluding line that expresses longing to revisit those holidays.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Memories of Summer Holidays

Every summer my village seemed to wake up with the sun, spilling light over narrow lanes and the salt-scented shore. Days began with the soft cry of fishermen and the bright chatter of children racing down to the beach. We learned to swim in a protected cove, laughing when the waves tipped us over and cheering each small triumph. Mango trees bowed under heavy fruit, and afternoons were given up to the shade of a banyan, where naps mixed with the drone of distant cicadas. Markets offered ripe fruits and handmade toys; I learned to bargain and to carry my own small bundle home. Evenings were for running after fireflies, roasting corn, and listening to elders tell tales of the sea and monsoon storms. Monsoon rains turned dusty paths into slick ribbons and painted the fields a deep green, while the air filled with the earthy perfume of wet soil. Simple games, kite competitions, and shared meals tied us to friends and family. Those summers taught me curiosity, resilience, and a deep love for small, ordinary joys that still warm my memory on cold or busy days.

b Summer holidays brought a bright freedom: sunlit beaches, mango-scented afternoons, joyous play with friends, and long evenings of stories and starry skies that filled my heart with wonder and belonging.

c 1. Salty breeze on my face
2. Warm sand between my toes
3. Scent of ripe mangoes
4. Crackle of corn over an open flame
5. Earthy perfume of wet soil after rain

d I often long to return to those slow, sunlit summer days—to feel the warm sand again and hear the gentle rhythm of the sea that once held my childhood heart.

Explanation:
The solution provides a full composition (part a) that follows a clear narrative arc: setting (village and beach), daily activities (swimming, markets, naps), sensory details (smell, sound, touch), and reflection on lessons learned and emotions carried forward. Part b is a concise 30-word introduction capturing the mood and main images; it is deliberately vivid and compact to set the scene. Part c extracts five sensory-detail phrases used in the composition—these anchor the reader in specific perceptions (touch, smell, sound), which is a standard technique to make descriptive writing vivid. Part d offers a single-sentence conclusion expressing longing, which ties the personal memory to an emotional reflection. Together the parts model how to construct a short descriptive composition: begin with a striking intro, develop with concrete sensory details and a few specific anecdotes, and close with a reflective sentence that gives the piece emotional resonance. For a 200-word target, aim for a single focused topic, use varied sentence lengths, and pepper sensory phrases throughout to keep the writing engaging.

Question #145 (ID: 578721)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are preparing a school project on how digital technology is transforming learning across Bangladesh. Based on recent initiatives, classroom practices, and the needs of rural and urban communities, complete the following tasks to present a clear picture of digital education in the country.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition titled "Digital Education in Bangladesh."
b. List five concrete achievements linked to digital education in Bangladesh (each as one short sentence).
c. Identify three major challenges to expanding digital education and propose one practical solution for each challenge.
d. Write one concluding sentence that captures the future vision of digital education in Bangladesh.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Digital Education in Bangladesh

Digital education in Bangladesh has emerged as a transformative force that expands learning beyond traditional classrooms. The government’s investments in ICT infrastructure, blended-learning initiatives, and digital content have made lessons more accessible to students in both cities and remote villages. Schools now use digital classrooms, online platforms, and multimedia resources to engage learners with visual and interactive content, while teachers receive training to integrate technology into lessons. During crises such as the COVID-19 pandemic, online classes and televised lessons ensured continuity of education. Mobile phones and low-cost tablets provide many students with study tools, interactive apps, and access to e-books. Initiatives like nationwide e-learning portals, ICT clubs, and partnerships with NGOs have encouraged digital literacy, computer skills, and coding among youth, preparing them for a knowledge-based economy. Despite ongoing gaps in connectivity and power supply, community centers and public Wi‑Fi hotspots are beginning to bridge divides. With sustained investment in teacher training, localized content, and affordable devices, digital education can promote equitable learning, reduce dropout rates, and equip Bangladeshi students with the skills needed for the 21st century.

b List of achievements
1. Nationwide rollout of digital classrooms and multimedia teaching in many public schools.
2. Launch of government e-learning portals offering free lessons and resources.
3. Expansion of mobile-based learning and educational apps reaching rural students.
4. Integration of ICT into school curricula and establishment of ICT clubs.
5. Continuity of education during the COVID-19 pandemic through online classes and televised lessons.

c Challenges and solutions
1) Challenge: Unequal internet access and weak connectivity in rural areas. Solution: Expand subsidized broadband and community Wi‑Fi hubs, and incentivize telecom operators to build rural infrastructure.
2) Challenge: Low digital literacy among teachers and caregivers. Solution: Implement scalable teacher training programs combining in-person workshops and short online certifications with follow-up mentoring.
3) Challenge: High cost and limited availability of devices for poor households. Solution: Launch device‑loan schemes through schools, public-private partnerships to supply low-cost tablets, and repair centers to extend device life.

d Concluding sentence
With inclusive policies, sustained investment, and community partnerships, digital education will empower every Bangladeshi learner to thrive in a connected, knowledge-driven future.

Explanation:
The composition (a) was structured to introduce the topic, describe key initiatives (digital classrooms, e-portals, mobile learning), mention the pandemic’s role, and conclude with forward-looking remarks—this mirrors effective short essay structure and stays within the requested scope. The achievements (b) are concise, verifiable outcomes commonly reported for Bangladesh’s digital education push. The challenges (c) identify three widely recognized barriers—connectivity, teacher capacity, and device access—and pair each with practical, scalable solutions grounded in policy and programmatic practice (infrastructure investment, teacher training, device programs). The concluding sentence (d) distills the vision: equity through collaboration and investment. Together, these responses give a coherent, classroom-ready presentation of how digital education is evolving in Bangladesh and what concrete steps can advance it further.

Options:
a. Write an e-mail to your class teacher requesting him/her to excuse your absence and briefly explain the reason.
b. Write a short note asking the teacher to provide the homework and class notes you missed, and mention any deadlines you are concerned about.
c. Write a polite request to the teacher asking permission to retake the quiz you missed, suggesting a convenient date and offering any documentation if required.
d. Write a brief apology message to your group partner explaining your absence from the group activity and offering how you will make up your part.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Answer:
To: classteacher@your-school.edu

Subject: Request to Excuse My Absence on [date]

Dear Sir/Madam,

I hope you are well. I am writing to inform you that I was absent from school on [date] due to a sudden family emergency that required my immediate attention. I apologize for missing class and any inconvenience this may have caused.

I kindly request you to excuse my absence for that day. I will make every effort to catch up with the lessons I missed.

Sincerely,

[Your Name]
Class [Your Class], Roll: [Your Roll Number]

b Answer:
Dear Sir/Madam,

Yours faithfully,

[Your Name]

c Answer:
Dear Sir/Madam,

I learned that a short quiz took place on [date], which I missed because of the family emergency. I respectfully request permission to retake the quiz at a time convenient for you. I am available on [suggested date(s) and time(s)] and can come before or after school if that helps. If you require any documentation about my absence, I will be glad to provide it.

Thank you for considering my request.

Hi [Partner's Name],

I am really sorry I missed our group activity on [date]. A family emergency came up unexpectedly and I could not join. I feel bad about letting you down. Please tell me if you want me to change anything or take on extra work to make up for it.

Apologetically,

[Your Name]

Explanation:
This set of responses uses polite, formal language appropriate for communication with a teacher and a slightly more personal but still responsible tone for communicating with a classmate.

a) The email to the teacher includes the essential elements: recipient (To), subject line, a brief reason for absence (family emergency), a clear request to excuse the absence, and a polite closing with the student's identification (class and roll). b) The note requesting homework and notes specifies the date missed and highlights any deadlines of concern. It offers practical options (collect physical copies or receive scanned versions) so the teacher can respond efficiently.

c) The quiz-retake request is polite and proactive: it states the missed assessment, asks for permission rather than demanding, suggests possible dates/times, and offers to provide documentation. That makes it easier for the teacher to accommodate the request.

d) The apology to the group partner acknowledges the absence, offers a concrete plan to make up the work with specific deadlines and meeting times, and invites the partner to request further adjustments. This shows responsibility and helps repair trust.

Tone and structure: For teacher communications use formal salutations (Dear Sir/Madam), clear subject lines, and respectful closings. For peers, use a courteous informal tone but keep commitments specific. Always provide dates and contact details where relevant so the recipient can act promptly.

Question #147 (ID: 578716)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are a teacher assigning a class task about renewable energy applications in villages. Students must demonstrate practical understanding and creative planning for sustainable electrification in rural communities.

Options:
a. Write a composition titled "Innovative Renewable Energy Solutions for Rural Communities" in exactly 200 words.
b. List five key benefits of adopting renewable energy in rural development (short phrases).
c. Identify three major challenges to implementing renewable energy systems in rural areas and provide one practical solution for each challenge.
d. Propose two small-scale community project ideas (provide a title and a two-line implementation plan for each).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Composition: Innovative Renewable Energy Solutions for Rural Communities

Access to reliable, affordable energy remains a cornerstone for development in rural areas. Implementing innovative renewable energy solutions—such as microgrids powered by solar panels, hybrid wind-solar systems, small-scale hydro, and biomass digesters—can transform livelihoods while protecting the environment. Solar home systems combined with battery storage provide immediate lighting, phone charging, and refrigeration for vaccines and perishables. Community microgrids managed by local cooperatives can ensure fair distribution and maintenance, while pay-as-you-go mobile payments lower upfront costs. Hybridizing resources increases reliability during seasonal variations: wind complements sun at night or during cloudy periods, and small hydro or biomass fills supply gaps. Training programs create local technicians, fostering employment and ensuring long-term operation. Integrating energy-efficient appliances and smart meters reduces waste and optimizes usage. Financing models blending government grants, microcredit, and private investment make projects scalable. Environmental benefits include reduced greenhouse gas emissions and lower indoor air pollution compared with kerosene. Social impacts encompass improved healthcare, education, and small enterprise growth. For sustainable adoption, projects must be community-led, culturally sensitive, and paired with education and maintenance plans. With the right mix of technology, finance, and governance, renewable energy can catalyze resilient rural development and shared prosperity.

b Benefits:
1. Reduced greenhouse gas emissions
2. Improved health from cleaner indoor air
3. Enhanced education and healthcare services
4. Local job creation and skills development
5. Energy independence and economic resilience

c Challenges and solutions:
1) Challenge: High initial capital costs — Solution: Use blended finance (grants + microloans + pay-as-you-go) to lower upfront barriers.
2) Challenge: Lack of technical skills and maintenance capacity — Solution: Implement local training programs and create technician cooperatives for operations and upkeep.
3) Challenge: Intermittent resource availability (sun/wind seasonality) — Solution: Deploy hybrid systems (solar+wind+storage or small hydro/biomass backup) and demand-side management to ensure reliability.

d Project ideas:
1) Solar-Powered Cold Storage Hub: Install a community-scale solar array with battery-backed cold rooms near farm markets; farmers rent space to store perishables, reducing post-harvest loss and increasing incomes. Train local operators for maintenance and management.
2) Microgrid for Artisan Workshops: Build a microgrid combining rooftop solar and a biomass generator to power tools and lighting for cottage industries; establish a cooperative to collect fees, schedule use, and provide technical training to artisans.

Explanation:
The composition (a) was written to balance practical technologies (solar, wind, hydro, biomass), social elements (cooperatives, training), finance and governance, and clear developmental outcomes, and adjusted to exactly 200 words. The benefits (b) highlight environmental, health, economic, social, and resilience outcomes commonly observed in rural renewable deployments. For challenges (c), the selected barriers—capital, skills, and intermittency—are typical impediments; each proposed solution is practical and commonly used: blended finance eases upfront costs, localized training ensures sustainability, and hybridization plus storage addresses reliability. The project ideas (d) are small-scale, replicable, and directly tied to local income generation: a cold storage hub tackles food loss and market value, while a microgrid for artisans enables productive electricity use and cooperative governance. Overall, the solutions emphasize community ownership, appropriate technology, scalable finance models, and capacity building—core principles for successful rural renewable energy adoption.

Dear Sir,

I am Arif, a student of Class VI, Roll No. 12. I would like to draw your kind attention to the fact that our school does not have a safe source of drinking water. Many students suffer from stomach problems and dehydration due to the unclean water available during school hours.

Therefore, I respectfully request you to arrange for a good water filter or water cooler and ensure a regular supply of clean drinking water for the students. If possible, a maintenance schedule and a small committee of teachers and students to look after the system may be formed to keep the water source hygienic.

I hope you will consider our request sympathetically and take immediate steps to protect the health of the students.

Yours obediently,

Arif
Class VI, Roll No. 12

b
Subject: Request for installation of a water filter and provision of clean drinking water.

c
1. Clean drinking water will prevent water-borne diseases and reduce student absenteeism.
2. A water filter ensures hygienic water during school hours when students cannot access safe water from home.
3. Providing safe water promotes a healthy learning environment and improves concentration and performance.

d
Yours obediently,

Arif
Class VI, Roll No. 12

Explanation:
The application includes the standard parts: date, recipient address, clear subject line, polite salutation, a concise description of the problem, a respectful plea for action, suggested practical measure (filter and maintenance), and a courteous closing with the student's name and class. The subject in (b) summarizes the request so the headmaster immediately understands the purpose. The three reasons in (c) focus on health, accessibility, and the impact on learning — the strongest points to persuade school authorities. The closing and signature in (d) follow typical formal-letter conventions used by students ("Yours obediently," then name and class/roll) to show respect and to identify the applicant for follow-up.

Question #151 (ID: 578707)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You have been asked by your school magazine to prepare several short items about a season that inspires you. Use the prompts below to create a main composition, a brief summary, vivid sensory notes, and a vocabulary box suitable for young readers.

Options:
a. Write a composition of about 200 words titled "The Season That Inspires Me".
b. Write a 30-word summary of the composition.
c. List five vivid sensory details (one for each sense) that appear in the season.
d. Choose three interesting words from your composition and give simple definitions for each.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a The Season That Inspires Me (Autumn)
Autumn is the season that quietly inspires me the most. After the intense heat of summer, the air cools to a gentle warmth, and mornings arrive wrapped in mist and soft sunlight. Leaves turn into a tapestry of amber, crimson, and gold, falling in slow, graceful dances that carpet roads and parks. Farmers reap their harvests, and markets fill with pumpkins, apples, and maize—baskets bursting with color and the smell of earth. Birds gather and call to one another as they prepare for long journeys, while small animals busy themselves in hurried preparations for winter. There is a calm rhythm to autumn: school bells ring with renewed energy, festivals bring families together, and evenings invite quiet walks under the clear, starlit sky. The season encourages reflection; it teaches that change can be beautiful and that endings often lead to rest and renewal. For me, autumn is both comforting and motivating. It awakens creativity, stirs memories, and reminds me to appreciate simple pleasures like a warm drink, a favorite book, or the crunch of leaves beneath my feet. In autumn’s gentle pause I find space to think, to dream, and to plan for the months ahead.

b 30-word summary:
Autumn brings cool air, colorful leaves, harvested abundance, and calm rhythms. It inspires reflection and creativity, blending family festivals and quiet moments, reminding us that beautiful change prepares us for renewal.

c Five sensory details:
- Sight: A carpet of amber and crimson leaves drifting down quiet streets.
- Sound: The dry, crisp rustle of leaves underfoot.
- Smell: Sweet, spicy scent of baked apple and cinnamon from kitchen windows.
- Taste: Warm, slightly tangy apple cider sipped on a chilly afternoon.
- Touch: The soft, cool brush of a light wind against your cheek.

d Vocabulary words with simple definitions:
- Tapestry: A rich, colorful pattern or scene, like a picture made of many threads (used for autumn leaves).
- Harvest: The gathering of crops when they are ready to be collected from the fields.
- Mist: A fine spray of tiny water droplets in the air that makes the morning look soft and slightly hazy.

Explanation:
The composition focuses on autumn because it offers strong, relatable imagery and emotional tones—change, reflection, and gentle renewal—that suit a short, descriptive essay. Paragraphs move from general atmosphere to specific scenes (colors, harvest, animals, festivals) and conclude with personal reflection to connect feeling and meaning.

The 30-word summary condenses the main themes: sensory atmosphere, inspiration, and the balance between activity (harvest, festivals) and calm (reflection). It captures the essay’s gist for a magazine blurb.

Sensory details were chosen to cover all five senses, making the scene vivid: visual (leaves), auditory (rustle), olfactory (baked apple), gustatory (cider), and tactile (cool wind). These help readers imagine autumn more fully.

Vocabulary words were selected because they appear naturally in autumn descriptions and are useful for young readers. Each definition is simple and concrete to aid comprehension and classroom use. The overall structure (composition, summary, sensory notes, vocabulary) is practical for both magazine layout and educational activities.

Question #152 (ID: 578709)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: A city planner asks you to provide a short composition and follow-up analysis about Traffic Congestion and Commuter Life in Dhaka. Use the context below to complete the four tasks.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition on "Traffic Congestion and Commuter Life in Dhaka."
b. List five major causes of traffic congestion in Dhaka (short phrases).
c. Give three immediate (short-term) measures and three long-term strategies to reduce congestion.
d. Write one persuasive concluding sentence urging urgent action.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Traffic Congestion and Commuter Life in Dhaka

Dhaka’s roads reflect a city bursting at the seams. Every morning and evening millions of commuters endure slow-moving lines of buses, cars, rickshaws and microbuses. The scarcity of organized public transport forces many to depend on overcrowded vehicles; this wastes time, raises stress, and reduces productivity. Children miss preparatory hours, and workers arrive late, affecting businesses and household incomes. The constant idling of engines increases fuel consumption and releases toxic pollutants, worsening public health. Emergency services often struggle as ambulances and fire engines cannot navigate blocked streets. Informal vendors and inconsistent parking further narrow the carriageways, while poor route planning and weak enforcement of traffic rules allow chaos to persist. Yet solutions exist: expanding reliable mass transit like metro rail and dedicated bus lanes can shift commuters away from private vehicles. Upgrading traffic management with synchronized signals, better signage, and trained officers can streamline flow. Encouraging non-motorized travel by creating safe sidewalks and cycleways will reduce short trips by motor vehicles. Public awareness campaigns and strict anti-illegal parking measures will improve discipline. Coordinated urban planning that integrates land use with transport investments is essential to restore mobility, protect health, and support Dhaka’s growth.

b Five major causes:
1. Rapid increase of private vehicles
2. Insufficient and unreliable public transport
3. Illegal parking and roadside vending
4. Narrow roads and poor road design
5. Weak traffic enforcement and rule violations

c Short-term measures (immediate):
1. Strict enforcement against illegal parking and loading/unloading in busy corridors.
2. Implement temporary dedicated bus lanes on major routes and prioritize bus movements during peak hours.
3. Deploy traffic marshals and use real-time traffic signaling to improve flow at key junctions.

Long-term strategies:
1. Expand mass transit (metro, BRT) and integrate ticketing to make public transport reliable and attractive.
2. Reconfigure urban land use with transit-oriented development and build more arterial roads and flyovers where appropriate.
3. Invest in non-motorized infrastructure (continuous sidewalks, protected cycle lanes) and multimodal hubs to reduce short motorized trips.

d Concluding sentence:
Dhaka cannot afford further delay—coordinated investment in mass transit, strict enforcement, and people-centered planning must begin now to restore mobility, protect health, and sustain the city’s future.

Explanation:
Explanation:

a) Composition: The 200-word composition was written to capture the daily realities of commuters, the social and economic impacts, environmental consequences, and a concise set of solutions. It balances problem description with actionable remedies and ends with a call for integrated planning. The word count was controlled by structuring paragraphs tightly and ensuring the final sentence uses precise phrasing to meet the 200-word requirement.

b) Causes: The five listed causes reflect frequently observed and reported factors in Dhaka: vehicle growth outpacing infrastructure, unreliable public transport pushing people into private or informal vehicles, street-level obstructions like illegal parking and vendors reducing effective road width, constrained road geometry and design, and ineffective enforcement that allows rule violations to persist.

c) Measures and strategies: Short-term measures prioritize actions that can quickly improve traffic flow and demonstrate benefits (enforcement, bus lanes, traffic marshals). Long-term strategies focus on systemic shifts (mass transit expansion, land-use coordination, non-motorized infrastructure) that reduce demand for private vehicles and provide sustainable mobility. Each recommendation links to common planning best practices and is tailored to Dhaka’s dense urban context.

d) Concluding sentence: The final sentence is concise and persuasive, stressing urgency and the three pillars—investment, enforcement, and people-centered planning—needed to achieve improvement.

Together, the answers form a coherent, actionable brief suitable for a city planner, student, or community advocate addressing Dhaka’s congestion challenges.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You have been asked to prepare content for the school's monthly newsletter on the theme "Role and Responsibilities of a Student". Provide the requested items below to help guide and inspire your classmates.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition titled "Responsibilities of a Student".
b. List five essential duties of a student; give a one-sentence explanation for each duty.
c. Compose a 30-word concluding paragraph that motivates students to practise these duties daily.
d. Suggest three practical activities students can organize to serve their school and local community, with a one-sentence description for each.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Responsibilities of a Student

A student’s years in school are a foundation for life, forming habits of mind, character, and civic duty. Foremost, a student must be devoted to learning by attending classes regularly, listening attentively, completing assignments on time, and preparing sincerely for examinations. Equally important are honesty and discipline; cheating, laziness, and indiscipline undermine both personal growth and communal trust. Respect for teachers, parents, and classmates fosters a positive environment where ideas can be shared and talents developed. A student should also care for physical and mental well-being through healthy routines, balanced study, and recreation. Participation in school activities—such as clubs, sports, and cultural events—builds teamwork, leadership, and creativity. Beyond the school gates, students owe duties to their community: helping in cleanliness drives, aiding the needy, and promoting awareness about social issues. Developing empathy and a sense of responsibility early makes one a better citizen tomorrow. By embracing curiosity, perseverance, and service, students not only prepare for successful careers but also contribute to a fairer and more compassionate society.

b Five essential duties:
1. Study diligently — to gain knowledge and develop critical thinking that shapes future choices.
2. Respect elders and teachers — to maintain harmony and benefit from their guidance and experience.
3. Be honest — to build trust and strong moral character in academic and personal life.
4. Keep the environment clean — to promote health and civic pride in school and community.
5. Help others — to cultivate empathy and contribute positively to society.

c Concluding paragraph (30 words):
Let every student embrace learning, integrity, respect, and service; these habits formed today will light the path to personal success and a stronger, kinder community tomorrow.

d Three practical activities:
1. School clean-up drives — organize monthly events where students clean classrooms, playgrounds, and nearby streets to promote hygiene and responsibility.
2. Peer tutoring program — pair older students with younger ones for regular study sessions to improve learning outcomes and mentorship.
3. Community awareness camps — conduct short workshops on health, recycling, or road safety to educate residents and practice civic leadership.

Explanation:
The composition (a) emphasizes balanced development: academic diligence, moral qualities, health, extracurricular involvement, and community service—key areas that define a student's responsibilities. The five duties in (b) are chosen because they cover intellectual, ethical, environmental, and social dimensions; each one-sentence explanation links the duty to its broader purpose. The 30-word conclusion (c) is concise and motivational, summarizing core values students should adopt. The three activities in (d) are practical, low-cost, and replicable: clean-up drives teach civic pride, peer tutoring reinforces knowledge and builds leadership, and awareness camps allow students to apply learning to real-world issues. Together these elements create a coherent set of materials suitable for a newsletter: they inform, guide behavior, and offer actionable steps for student involvement.

Question #154 (ID: 578711)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are a member of your school's environmental club launching a "School Garden Project" to promote biodiversity, hands-on learning, and sustainable habits. Prepare materials and plans that the club can use to present the project to the school and the local community.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition titled "School Garden Project" describing the purpose, activities, and expected outcomes.
b. List five key environmental and educational benefits of a school garden (short bullet points).
c. Describe step-by-step how to plant and maintain three suitable native species (specify species type and give practical care tips for each).
d. Propose three practical ways to involve the wider community and two measurable metrics to evaluate the project's success over one year.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a School Garden Project
The school garden project is a hands-on initiative where students, teachers, and community volunteers create and care for a living outdoor classroom. Its purpose is to teach ecology, nutrition, and responsibility through practical activities like seed-starting, composting, and seasonal planting. Weekly garden club sessions will combine lessons on plant life cycles, pollinators, and soil health with active tasks: preparing beds, sowing seeds, watering, and harvesting. Planned features include a native pollinator patch, a small fruit/vegetable plot for the cafeteria, labeled learning stations, and a compost corner. The garden will host workshops for parents and neighborhood residents to share gardening skills and recipes using harvests. Expected outcomes after one year are increased student engagement in science, a modest supply of fresh produce for the school kitchen, improved local biodiversity evidenced by visiting insects and birds, and strengthened community ties. The project emphasizes low-cost, low-tech methods—mulch, rainwater harvesting, and organic pest control—so it remains sustainable and replicable at other schools.b Key benefits:
- Hands-on science education: living examples of biology and ecology.
- Improved nutrition: fresh produce for meals and demonstrations.
- Biodiversity support: habitat for pollinators and native species.
- Mental and physical health: outdoor activity reduces stress.
- Environmental stewardship: builds lifelong sustainable habits.c Planting and maintenance of three native species:
1) Native fruit tree (e.g., a local dwarf apple or mango depending on region)
   - Planting: choose sunny, well-drained site; dig hole twice the root-ball width; mix native soil with compost.
   - Care: water deeply once weekly first year; mulch to retain moisture; prune dead branches in dormant season; protect from pests with netting when fruiting.
   - Maintenance tips: stake young trees for support; fertilize lightly in spring.
2) Native flowering shrub (e.g., butterfly bush or native dogwood)
   - Planting: partial to full sun; soil amended with compost; space according to mature size.
   - Care: regular watering until established; deadhead spent blooms to encourage more flowers; prune after flowering.
   - Maintenance tips: plant in clusters to attract pollinators; avoid overwatering.
3) Native groundcover/vegetable patch (e.g., clover groundcover or leafy greens like spinach/kale)
   - Planting: prepare shallow beds with loamy soil; sow seeds at recommended depth and spacing.
   - Care: keep evenly moist until germination; thin seedlings to prevent overcrowding; mulch to suppress weeds.
   - Maintenance tips: rotate crops seasonally; use companion planting to deter pests.
d Community involvement and metrics:
- Involvement:
  1. Host monthly open-garden days with hands-on volunteer shifts and short workshops for residents.
  2. Partner with local businesses and farmers for seed/soil donations and expert talks.
  3. Create student-led outreach: social media updates, a newsletter, and seasonal produce stands where proceeds support garden supplies.
- Metrics (to evaluate after one year):
  1. Survival and productivity metric: percentage of planted specimens surviving and total kilograms of produce harvested.
  2. Engagement and education metric: number of volunteers and participants in workshops plus pre/post surveys showing increased knowledge or interest in gardening.

Explanation:
This solution is structured to give a project-ready composition, concise benefit points, practical species-specific planting and care instructions, and realistic community engagement plus measurable outcomes. The 200-word composition provides a clear project overview and expected impacts while emphasizing low-cost, sustainable methods. The benefits list focuses on both environmental and educational gains that schools commonly aim for. For species care, one fruit tree, one flowering shrub, and one groundcover/vegetable patch are chosen to cover different garden layers and functions (food, habitat, soil coverage). Steps include site selection, soil preparation, watering, mulching, pruning, and pest protection—fundamental practices that apply to most native plants but are noted with specific actions for each type. Community involvement ideas (open days, partnerships, student outreach) are practical ways schools expand resources and foster ownership. The two metrics—survival/productivity and engagement/education—are measurable with simple records (harvest logs, attendance lists, surveys) and give a balanced view of ecological and social success.

Question #155 (ID: 578697)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Bangladesh faces a growing challenge of youth unemployment and skill mismatch. Consider the situation of recent graduates, rural migrants, and small entrepreneurs who struggle to find stable employment. Use this context to respond to the following tasks.

Options:
a. Write a composition on "Youth Unemployment and Skill Mismatch in Bangladesh" in 200 words.
b. Mention four primary causes of youth unemployment in Bangladesh (brief points).
c. List four major social or economic effects of prolonged youth unemployment (brief points).
d. Suggest four practical solutions or interventions that can reduce youth unemployment (brief points with one-sentence rationale each).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Unemployment among the youth in Bangladesh has become a pressing national concern. Although the economy has grown, job creation has not kept pace with the rising number of graduates and young job-seekers. Structural mismatches between education and labor-market needs, limited industrial diversification, seasonal agriculture, and urban migration intensify the problem. Many young people possess theoretical degrees but lack practical skills demanded by employers. As a result, underemployment and informal work expand, while promising entrepreneurs face difficulties obtaining finance and markets. The social consequences are severe: rising frustration, delaying marriage, increased crime risk, and loss of productive potential. Women and rural youth are particularly vulnerable, widening inequality. Addressing youth unemployment requires integrated policies: reforming education to emphasize technical and vocational training, promoting small and medium enterprises through credit and incubation, incentivizing labor-intensive industries, and strengthening digital and entrepreneurship skills. Public-private partnerships can align curricula with employer needs and facilitate apprenticeships. Local governments should support rural employment through agro-processing and infrastructure. Transparent recruitment and robust social safety nets can ease transitions. With targeted investments and long-term planning, Bangladesh can turn its youthful population into a demographic dividend rather than a liability. Collective action by citizens, NGOs and government will be essential now.

b 1) Skill-education mismatch: curricula emphasize theory over practical and technical skills.
2) Limited quality job creation: slow industrial diversification and insufficient labor-intensive industries.
3) Population pressure and graduate inflow: more entrants to the labor market than available formal jobs.
4) Informal recruitment barriers and weak access to finance: nepotism, limited job information, and lack of startup capital.

c 1) Increased poverty and income insecurity among households.
2) Social problems: frustration, mental health issues, and higher risk of crime.
3) Brain drain: skilled youth migrate for work, reducing local human capital.
4) Economic inefficiency: wasted human potential and slower economic development.

d 1) Revise education and training: expand vocational and technical programs aligned with industry needs — improves employability quickly.
2) Support SMEs and startups: accessible credit, incubators, and market linkages — creates local jobs and entrepreneurship pathways.
3) Promote apprenticeships and industry partnerships: formalize on-the-job training and internships — bridges theory and practice.
4) Invest in labor-intensive sectors and rural value chains: agro-processing, light manufacturing, digital services — spreads job opportunities beyond cities.

Explanation:
The composition (part a) summarizes the problem, causes, consequences, and an integrated policy response. It was written to stay within a 200-word target and to highlight both structural and immediate factors. For part b, the selected causes focus on supply-side (skills, graduates) and demand-side (job creation, access) constraints that are repeatedly cited in labour-market analyses. Part c lists consequences that are direct results of sustained unemployment: individual, social, and macroeconomic impacts. Part d offers actionable interventions: education reform to fix the skill mismatch, SME/startup support to expand demand for labor, apprenticeships to connect young people to employers, and targeted investment in labor-absorbing sectors — each intervention includes a brief rationale to show how it addresses a specific cause. Together these answers present a coherent diagnosis and set of responses suitable for policy discussion, NGO programs, or school-level essays on the topic.

Question #156 (ID: 578698)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are students of Riverdale High School. There is a small, unused triangular plot beside the science laboratory that is full of weeds. You and your classmates want to transform it into a small medicinal-herb and pollinator garden to support environmental education and attract beneficial insects. Prepare the required documents and plans.

Options:
a. Write a formal application to the Headmaster requesting allotment of the triangular plot for the medicinal-herb and pollinator garden.
b. List five essential materials/tools you will need to start and maintain the garden, with a one-line purpose for each item.
c. Draft a simple three-month work plan (week-by-week or month-by-month) with tasks and who will be responsible.
d. Describe four educational and environmental benefits this garden will provide to the students and the school.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
23 September 2025

To

The Headmaster

Riverdale High School

Subject: Request for allotment of the triangular plot beside the science laboratory for a medicinal-herb and pollinator garden

Dear Sir/Madam,

We, the students of Class VIII and the Science Club of Riverdale High School, respectfully draw your kind attention to a small triangular plot located beside the science laboratory which is currently unused and overgrown with weeds. With your permission, we wish to convert this space into a medicinal-herb and pollinator garden.

This garden will serve as a living laboratory where students can learn about plant biology, herbal remedies, pollination, and sustainable gardening practices. It will also attract bees, butterflies, and other pollinators that are important for local biodiversity. We propose to carry out all initial planting and subsequent maintenance activities during school hours under teacher supervision. We will ensure cleanliness, regular upkeep, and safe use of the space.

Therefore, we humbly request you to kindly allot the triangular plot beside the science laboratory to the students for this purpose and grant permission to begin work from the first week of October.

Yours faithfully,

(Representative) Arif Rahman
On behalf of Class VIII and the Science Club
Riverdale High School

b
1. Spade and hand trowels — For digging, soil preparation, and planting seedlings.
2. Mulch (straw/wood chips) — To conserve moisture, suppress weeds, and improve soil health.
3. Native medicinal herb seedlings/seeds (e.g., mint, basil, holy basil, lemongrass) — Plants to establish the herb garden and demonstrate medicinal uses.
4. Watering can/hoses with nozzle — For efficient watering and seedling care.
5. Bee- and butterfly-friendly flowering plants (e.g., marigold, cosmos) and a simple bee house — To attract and support pollinators.

c
Three-month work plan (October–December)

October (Preparation & Planting)
- Week 1: Clear weeds and debris; measure and mark beds (Responsibility: Science Club members supervised by Science teacher).
- Week 2: Prepare soil (turn soil, add compost), make basic pathways (Responsibility: Volunteer students + caretaker).
- Week 3: Plant hardy herbs and flowering plants; install simple signs labeling species (Responsibility: Gardening team of students).
- Week 4: Mulch beds; set up a watering schedule and assign weekly monitors (Responsibility: Class VIII monitors).

November (Establishment & Monitoring)
- Week 1–2: Monitor watering, remove any new weeds, replace failed seedlings if needed (Responsibility: Assigned student team).
- Week 3: Begin informal weekly observations and record plant growth in a garden log (Responsibility: Science Club).
- Week 4: Install a small bee house and observe pollinator visits; share findings at a short assembly (Responsibility: Science teacher + students).

December (Maintenance & Educational Activities)
- Week 1–2: Prune and harvest small amounts where appropriate for classroom demonstrations (Responsibility: Science Club under teacher supervision).
- Week 3: Prepare simple posters on medicinal uses and pollinator importance; display near garden (Responsibility: Art & Science teams).
- Week 4: Review the three-month progress, plan winter protection if needed, and schedule ongoing care (Responsibility: Garden committee).

d
Four benefits to students and the school:
1. Hands-on learning: Students gain practical knowledge of plant life cycles, ecology, and basic horticulture that complements classroom science lessons.
2. Environmental stewardship: The garden encourages responsibility, teamwork, and an ethic of caring for living systems, fostering long-term conservation habits.
3. Pollinator support and biodiversity: Flowering plants and a bee house provide habitat and food for pollinators, improving local biodiversity and ecosystem health.
4. Health and well-being: Interaction with green space reduces stress, promotes outdoor activity, and offers knowledge of safe, locally available medicinal herbs for simple first-aid demonstrations.

Explanation:
This solution provides a complete set of deliverables aligned with the scenario. The application (part a) follows formal letter structure (date, recipient, subject, salutation, purpose, polite request, closing and signature) so it can be submitted directly to the Headmaster. The materials list (part b) focuses on essential, low-cost items that address soil preparation, planting, watering, mulch for moisture/weeds, and pollinator support. The three-month plan (part c) breaks tasks into realistic weekly steps with clear responsibilities to ensure the project is manageable for students and staff; it includes preparation, planting, monitoring, and educational outreach. The benefits (part d) highlight pedagogical, environmental, and health advantages to justify the request and help persuade the Headmaster. Together these parts present a practical, educational, and sustainable proposal for converting unused school land into a productive learning garden.

Question #157 (ID: 578700)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: You are asked to prepare a short composition and related notes about 'Urbanization and Population Pressure in Dhaka' that examines causes, effects, and practical remedies for the city's growing population stress.

Options:
a. Write a composition of about 200 words on 'Urbanization and Population Pressure in Dhaka'.
b. List three major causes of population pressure in Dhaka with brief explanations.
c. Propose four practical solutions to reduce urban population pressure, suitable for local communities.
d. Describe four concrete steps the government can take in the next five years to manage Dhaka's population pressure effectively.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Composition (about 200 words): Dhaka, the capital city of Bangladesh, has grown into a bustling metropolis driven by rural-to-urban migration, economic opportunity, and rapid industrialization. As people flock to the city seeking jobs, education, and better services, Dhaka faces severe population pressure that strains housing, transportation, sanitation, healthcare, and education systems. Informal settlements expand as low-income families settle in slums with limited access to clean water and sanitation. Traffic congestion and air pollution increase as road networks become inadequate for the rising number of commuters. Public hospitals and schools are overcrowded, reducing quality of services and widening social inequality. The environmental consequences include loss of green spaces, increased flooding risk from blocked drains, and higher waste generation with insufficient disposal systems. Addressing these challenges requires coordinated planning: developing affordable housing, decentralizing economic activities to reduce rural migration, investing in reliable public transport, and improving slum upgrading. Community awareness about family planning and women’s education also play key roles. If managed proactively with inclusive policies and sustainable urban design, Dhaka’s human resources can be transformed into a productive asset rather than an unbearable burden on the city’s infrastructure and environment.

b Three major causes (with brief explanations):
1. Rural-to-urban migration: People move to Dhaka seeking jobs, education, and services not available in rural areas.
2. Economic centralization: Concentration of industries, offices, and higher wages in Dhaka attracts workers from across the country.
3. Insufficient rural development and services: Lack of healthcare, education, and employment in villages pushes families toward the city.

c Four practical community-level solutions:
1. Promote local micro-enterprises and vocational training in peri-urban and rural areas to create jobs near people’s homes.
2. Support community-led slum upgrading (sanitation, drainage, secure tenure) to improve living conditions without forced evictions.
3. Encourage shared and non-motorized transport (bicycle lanes, pedestrian zones, community shuttle services) to reduce congestion.
4. Run local awareness programs on family planning, girls’ education, and small-family benefits through schools, mosques, and NGOs.

d Four concrete government steps for the next five years:
1. Decentralize economic policy: Incentivize industries to set up in secondary cities via tax breaks and infrastructure grants to reduce migration pressure on Dhaka.
2. Invest in mass public transport: Expand bus rapid transit and metro lines, complemented by regulated feeder services, to cut congestion and pollution.
3. Implement affordable housing programs: Build mixed-income housing and provide housing subsidies/vouchers to formalize settlements and reduce slums.
4. Strengthen family planning and female education: Fund accessible reproductive health services, enforce minimum marriage age, and ensure universal secondary schooling for girls.

Explanation:
The composition summarizes how urbanization and population influx strain Dhaka’s infrastructure and environment, and why coordinated interventions are necessary. The causes focus on push (lack of rural services) and pull (jobs in Dhaka) factors that drive migration. Community solutions emphasize job creation near homes, improving slum conditions, sustainable mobility, and reproductive health education — measures that are feasible locally and reduce immediate pressure. Government steps combine short- and medium-term structural policies: decentralizing economic activity reduces migration drivers; mass transit and affordable housing address infrastructure bottlenecks; and family planning and girls’ education reduce long-term population growth. Together, these approaches target both symptoms (congestion, slums) and root causes (unequal development, limited local opportunities) to produce sustainable relief for Dhaka’s population pressure.

Question:
Suppose, you are Aisha/Rakib, a student of class X. You are going to celebrate your birthday on 5th March. You will arrange a tea party along with a short cultural programme at your home. Now, perform the following tasks.

Options:
a. Write an informal invitation letter to your friend Jamil/Jamila inviting him/her to the birthday tea party and cultural programme.
b. Write the address panel (From, To and Stamp) to be put on the envelope.
c. Write two short persuasive sentences encouraging your friend to come and bring a small gift if possible.
d. Write the closing lines: a warm sign-off, your name and class.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
Dear Jamila,

Assalamu Alaikum. I hope you are doing well. I am very excited to tell you that I will celebrate my 16th birthday on 5th March. I am arranging a small tea party and a short cultural programme at my home. The celebration will start at 4:00 p.m. and will include a couple of songs and a short skit performed by my classmates. I would be very happy if you could come and join the celebration. Your presence will make the day more special to me.

Date: 5th March
Time: 4:00 p.m.
Venue: 12 Maple Lane, Green Park

Please come on time. Waiting to celebrate with you!

Yours lovingly,
Aisha (Class X)

b
Stamp
From:
Aisha
12 Maple Lane
Green Park, Dhaka-1212

To:
Jamila
34 Rose Avenue
Mirpur, Dhaka-1216

c
Please do come and celebrate with me — your company will make the party joyful. If you can, bring a small handmade or simple gift; it will mean a lot but your presence is the greatest gift.

d
With love and warm regards,
Aisha
Class: X

Explanation:
This solution follows the usual structure of an informal invitation letter and related items.

- For (a) the letter begins with a friendly salutation, states the occasion (16th birthday), gives the date, time and venue, and briefly describes the programme (tea party and cultural items). It includes a polite invitation sentence and a personal closing. These elements make the invitation clear and warm.

- For (b) the address panel lists the sender (From) and receiver (To) with full addresses and a place for the stamp. This is standard for an envelope: stamp in top-right, From in top-left or top-center of the back/left front, and To prominently in the center.

- For (c) the two persuasive sentences are short, affectionate and respectful. They emphasize that the friend's presence matters more than any gift but gently suggest bringing a small gift if possible. This balance is polite and typical for informal invites among friends.

- For (d) the closing includes a warm sign-off, the sender's name and class so the recipient recognises who invited them and their school level.

Tone: Because this is an informal letter between friends, the language is friendly and personal rather than fully formal. Key details (date, time, venue) are included so the friend can make plans. An RSVP request is implied by asking the friend to come on time; if required, an explicit line asking to confirm attendance could be added.
