Question #159 (ID: 578695)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are Riya/Raj. Your younger brother Arif seldom reads newspapers and thinks they are boring. You want to convince him that reading newspapers is useful for his studies, general knowledge, and future career. Prepare materials to persuade him and to help him start the habit.

Options:
a. Write a friendly letter to Arif explaining why he should start reading newspapers regularly. Use a persuasive but caring tone and include a few concrete suggestions (which section to start with, how much time to spend daily).
b. List and explain five specific benefits of reading newspapers that would appeal to a young student preparing for competitive exams and interviews.
c. Read the following short front-page news summary and write a concise 5–6 sentence paraphrase suitable for Arif that highlights the most important facts.

"The city council inaugurated the new riverside metro line on 1 September. Officials reported the line will cut commuter time by up to 30% and carry an estimated 200,000 passengers daily. The project faced delays due to funding shortages and technical issues but was completed after a revised budget and additional contractors were approved. Environment groups praised the plan for including green corridors along the route, while some local vendors worried about reduced foot traffic. The council promised ongoing support for affected businesses and launched a commuter awareness campaign."
d. Suggest a simple 7-day plan to help Arif begin a daily newspaper habit, including specific activities for each day and measurable goals.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
Dear Arif,

How are you? I hope everything is fine with you. I want to tell you something important — I think you would really benefit from reading a newspaper every day. I know you find it boring now, but let me explain why it’s worth trying and how you can make it easy and useful.

First, start small: spend just 15–20 minutes each morning or evening. Begin with the sections that are easiest and most interesting for you — for example, the sports page if you like sports, the national news for current events, or the education/career pages for exam updates and job tips. Read one main article and one editorial each day. Circle or underline new words and look them up later — this will improve your vocabulary for exams and interviews.

Newspapers give up-to-date information that you won’t get from textbooks, and they help with comprehension and critical thinking. To make it fun, we can discuss a short article every weekend; I will quiz you lightly on headlines or ask you to summarize a story in two sentences. Also, try reading news apps or the paper version — whichever suits you better.

Give this a two-week try. If you don’t like it after that, we’ll rethink the plan. I’m sure once you start, you’ll notice useful facts, better language, and more confidence in discussions and exams.

With love,
Riya/Raj

b
1) Current Affairs and Exam Edge — Newspapers provide latest events and government decisions, which are frequently asked in competitive exams and interviews. Regular reading builds a bank of facts to answer general knowledge questions.

2) Vocabulary and Language Skills — Exposure to well-edited articles improves word choice, reading speed, sentence structure, and writing style. This helps in essay-writing and comprehension sections.

3) Critical Thinking and Opinion Formation — Editorials and analysis teach how to weigh evidence and form balanced views, an important skill for interviews and group discussions.

4) Awareness of Career and Opportunities — Classifieds, education columns, and career pages list scholarships, exam notices, internships, and job openings that a student might miss otherwise.

5) Discussion and Interview Confidence — Being informed about current topics helps you speak confidently in class, during interviews, and in social situations; it shows curiosity and preparedness to examiners and employers.

c
Paraphrase for Arif:

The city council opened a new riverside metro line on 1 September that is expected to shorten commuting times by up to 30% and serve about 200,000 passengers each day. Although the project encountered delays because of funding and technical problems, it was finished after approving extra funds and contractors. Environmental groups welcomed the inclusion of green corridors along the route, but some local vendors are concerned that the new line will reduce their customer traffic. The council has promised support for affected businesses and launched a campaign to inform commuters about the new services.

d
7-Day Starter Plan

Day 1 — Orientation (Goal: 10–15 minutes): Browse the front page and headline summaries. Pick one article to read fully (national or interests). Note 3 interesting facts.

Day 2 — Section Focus (Goal: 15–20 minutes): Read the education/career or sports section. Write a one-sentence summary of one article and jot down two new words with meanings.

Day 3 — Vocabulary and Questions (Goal: 15–20 minutes): Read an editorial. List two opposing viewpoints mentioned and use one new word in a sentence.

Day 4 — Timed Reading (Goal: 15 minutes): Set a 15-minute timer. Read as much as you can and underline the main points. Share one takeaway with a family member.

Day 5 — Summarize (Goal: 20 minutes): Read one front-page article and write a 3–4 sentence summary in your own words.

Day 6 — Discuss (Goal: 20 minutes): Read a short article and discuss it with me or a friend for 5–10 minutes. Try to give an opinion and a supporting reason.

Day 7 — Review and Reflect (Goal: 20 minutes): Re-read notes from the week. Pick the most useful section for you and plan a daily 15–20 minute routine going forward. If you complete this week, reward yourself (small treat) and continue with the habit.

This gradual plan builds interest, vocabulary, and confidence without overwhelming you. Start with short, manageable tasks and increase time only after the habit forms.

Explanation:
This set of answers is designed to persuade and equip a young reader to start reading newspapers. 

For (a), the letter uses a friendly persuasive tone, practical suggestions (time, section choice), and a small accountability idea (discussing articles) to motivate the younger sibling. The structure follows a clear opening, body with specific advice, and a supportive closing.

For (b), the benefits are chosen to appeal directly to a student preparing for exams and interviews: current affairs knowledge, language improvement, critical thinking, opportunities, and confidence in discussions. Each benefit links to concrete outcomes valuable for academic and career advancement.

For (c), the paraphrase condenses the original news points into a clear, neutral summary: inauguration date, expected impact (commute reduction, passenger numbers), causes of delay and resolution, environmental response, vendor concerns, and council measures. This models how to extract and present key facts — a useful skill for note-taking and answering exam questions.

For (d), the 7-day plan uses very small, achievable daily goals that build reading stamina, summarization skills, vocabulary growth, and discussion practice. It emphasizes measurable outcomes (time, number of facts, summaries) and a review to consolidate the habit. The combination of short tasks and social accountability increases the chance Arif will maintain the habit beyond the first week.

Question #160 (ID: 578696)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
A wide seasonal canal runs along one side of your neighborhood. Every day many people — students, market-goers and the elderly — must cross it and face delays and danger because there is no safe crossing. The community wants immediate action to build a footbridge. Prepare the necessary written items to request, inform and support this project.

Options:
a. Write an application to the Mayor requesting construction of a footbridge over the canal (formal letter).
b. Draft a short public notice (50–60 words) informing residents about a community meeting to discuss the bridge project. Include date, time and venue.
c. Compose a brief recommendation (60–80 words) from the headmaster of the local school endorsing the bridge construction for student safety.
d. List four practical benefits the footbridge will provide to your locality, with one-line explanations for each.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
Date: 10 February 2025

To

The Mayor

Greenfield Municipal Corporation

Subject: Request for construction of a footbridge over the seasonal canal beside Oak Lane

Respected Sir,

I am a resident of Oak Lane, Greenfield, and write on behalf of the local residents' welfare committee. A wide seasonal canal runs along the eastern edge of our neighborhood. Each day hundreds of people — including schoolchildren, elderly residents and market-goers — must cross the canal at unsafe spots. There is no designated crossing, and many residents are forced to take long detours or risk slipping on muddy banks. Recently, two minor accidents involving children were reported.

In view of the daily hardship and the safety risk, we earnestly request that the Municipality arrange for the immediate construction of a sturdy footbridge at the central crossing point near Oak Lane and Market Road. A properly designed bridge with handrails and non-slip surface will ensure safe, quick and year-round crossing for all.

We shall be grateful if you could inspect the site and include this project in the municipal development plan at the earliest.

Yours faithfully,

Amina Rahman

Secretary, Oak Lane Residents' Welfare Committee

On behalf of the residents

Contact: 01234-567890

b
Notice:

A public meeting will be held on 20 February 2025 at 5:00 p.m. in the Oak Lane Community Hall to discuss construction of a footbridge over the canal. All residents, local shopkeepers and parents are requested to attend. Your suggestions and support are important.

Organizer: Oak Lane Residents' Welfare Committee

c
Recommendation (from Headmaster):

Date: 11 February 2025

To Whom It May Concern,

As Headmaster of Oak Lane Primary School, I strongly endorse the construction of a footbridge over the canal near our school. Many of our students cross this area daily and face dangerous conditions, especially during monsoon. A safe bridge will significantly reduce travel time, prevent accidents and ensure regular school attendance. I request the municipal authorities to prioritize this project for the safety of our children.

Sincerely,

Md. Harun Ahmed

Headmaster, Oak Lane Primary School

d
Four practical benefits:

1. Improved safety — A dedicated footbridge eliminates risky crossings and reduces slips, falls and water-related accidents.
2. Shorter travel time — Direct crossing saves time for students, workers and shoppers who currently detour long distances.
3. Increased school attendance — Safer access encourages regular attendance by children, especially during bad weather.
4. Economic convenience — Easier access to the market and services supports local businesses and daily-wage earners by reducing delays and transport costs.

Explanation:
a) Application: A formal request to the Mayor must state the problem (canal without safe crossing), give concrete examples (students, elderly, accidents), request a specific remedy (footbridge at central crossing), and offer local representation (residents' committee) and contact details. Including urgency and a call for inspection helps prompt action.

b) Notice: A community notice should be short and include essential details — purpose (discuss footbridge), date, time, venue and target audience (residents, parents). It should invite participation and emphasize that community input is important to show broad local support.

c) Recommendation: A headmaster's endorsement adds weight because it highlights the bridge's importance for children's safety and attendance. The recommendation should be concise, state the authority of the writer, describe the problem for students, and request prioritization by authorities.

d) Benefits: Each listed benefit ties directly to observed problems: safety (reducing accidents), time savings (removing detours), education (attendance), and local economy (easier market access). Clear one-line explanations show why the bridge is a practical investment.

Overall, these documents together (formal application, public notice and institutional endorsement) form a persuasive, organized approach to mobilize municipal action, demonstrate community support, and prioritize public safety.

Question #161 (ID: 578685)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
One of your classmates borrowed your comprehensive chemistry notes last month and has not returned them yet. Your final exam is approaching in two weeks and you urgently need the notes to revise. Draft communications and related items to request the return and explain why you need them.

Options:
a. Write an email (about 120–150 words) asking for the notes to be returned.
b. Write a short polite SMS reminder (one or two lines) you could send right away.
c. Rewrite the email in a more formal academic tone (about 80–100 words).
d. List three clear reasons why you need the notes back and state a reasonable deadline for their return.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
Answer:
To: rizwan@example.com
Subject: Kindly returning my chemistry notes

Dear Rizwan,

I hope you are doing well. I am writing to remind you about the chemistry notes you borrowed from me last month. My final exam starts in two weeks, and those notes contain the summaries and solved problems I rely on to revise effectively. I would be very grateful if you could bring them to class on Friday or let me know a convenient time for me to pick them up.

If you need more time, please tell me when you can return them. Thank you for your understanding and help.

Best regards,
Arun

b
Answer:
Hi Rizwan — hope you’re well. Could you please return my chemistry notes by Friday? I need them to prepare for the exam. Thanks a lot!

c
Answer:
To: rizwan@example.com
Subject: Request for Return of Chemistry Notes

Dear Mr. Rahman,

I hope this message finds you well. I am writing to request the return of the chemistry notes I lent you last month. My final examination commences in two weeks, and the notes are essential for my revision, particularly the consolidated summaries and problem solutions. Kindly inform me if you can bring them to campus by Friday or suggest an alternative time for collection.

Thank you for your cooperation.

Sincerely,
Arun Choudhury

d
Answer:
1) Time-sensitive revision: The exam is in two weeks, so I need the notes immediately to complete my study schedule.
2) Unique content: The notes include my annotated summaries and solved examples that are not available elsewhere.
3) Group obligations: I must prepare for a group discussion where I am presenting topics based on those notes.

Reasonable deadline: Please return the notes by next Friday (within seven days). If that is not possible, notify me of a specific day and time for pickup.

Explanation:
The email in (a) uses a polite, clear tone: subject line, greeting, context (borrowed notes), reason (exam in two weeks), request (return or arrange pickup), and closing. These elements make the request specific and courteous. The SMS in (b) is short and direct, suitable for instant reminders; it repeats the key information (need by Friday) and thanks the recipient. The formal rewrite in (c) increases formality with a more formal salutation, precise wording, and a courteous closing—appropriate for classmates you address more formally or for a tutor. The reasons in (d) are concrete and practical: showing urgency (time-sensitive), uniqueness (personal annotations), and additional obligations (group presentation) justifies a firm but reasonable deadline. Suggesting a clear deadline (next Friday) helps the borrower act promptly; offering an alternative (ask for a pickup time) keeps the tone cooperative.

Question #162 (ID: 578686)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Suppose you are Alex. Your younger brother Jordan stays up late and wastes hours playing mobile games, which is affecting his studies, sleep and mood. Now prepare responses to help him manage his time better and reduce gaming.

Options:
a. Write an informal letter to Jordan advising him to use his time wisely and reduce mobile gaming. (Approximately 120–150 words.)
b. Prepare a daily time schedule for Jordan (24-hour format) that balances study, rest, recreation and a limited gaming period.
c. List five negative effects of excessive mobile gaming on a student's life and three positive activities Jordan can adopt instead (brief explanations).
d. Convert the main points of the letter into six concise spoken talking-points Jordan can remember during a face-to-face conversation.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
Dear Jordan,
I hope you are doing well. I’ve noticed you spend many late hours on mobile games and it’s starting to affect your studies, sleep and mood. I’m writing because I care about you and want to help. Try to set a clear daily plan: finish homework first, then relax, and allow only a short, fixed gaming time in the evening. Aim for at least eight hours of sleep, regular meals and some outdoor activity each day. If a game makes you anxious or distracts you from important tasks, uninstall it or use app timers to limit play. Start small — reduce gaming by 30 minutes each week until it feels balanced. I’m here to support you and can help make a schedule or join you for a sport or hobby.
Take care,
Alex

b
Daily Schedule (24-hour format):
06:30 — Wake up and morning routine
07:00 — Breakfast
07:30–09:30 — Study / school preparation (focused work)
09:30–14:30 — School / classes
14:30–15:00 — Lunch and short rest
15:00–16:30 — Homework / revision
16:30–17:30 — Outdoor activity / exercise
17:30–18:30 — Free time (reading, family, hobby)
18:30–19:30 — Dinner and relax
19:30–20:00 — Light revision / plan next day
20:00–20:45 — Gaming (maximum 45 minutes) or social time
20:45–21:30 — Wind down (no screens) — read or meditate
22:30 — Bedtime
(Adjust weekends to include longer hobby/outing periods and reduced study blocks.)

c
Five negative effects of excessive mobile gaming:
1. Poor academic performance — Less time and concentration for homework and revision.
2. Sleep deprivation — Late-night gaming reduces sleep quality and daytime alertness.
3. Physical health issues — Eye strain, poor posture and reduced exercise.
4. Mood and social problems — Irritability, isolation from family/friends and reduced empathy.
5. Time management failure — Difficulty prioritizing responsibilities and forming good habits.

Three positive activities Jordan can adopt instead:
1. Regular exercise or a sport — Improves mood, energy and focus for studying.
2. A creative hobby (drawing, music, coding) — Builds skills, offers achievement and reduces screen dependency.
3. Study groups or tutoring — Makes learning social and more effective, reducing the temptation to escape into games.

d
Six concise talking-points for a face-to-face conversation:
1. "I care about you — your studies and health matter to me." 
2. "Gaming is fine in small doses, but it shouldn’t take over your day." 
3. "Let’s set a simple daily plan and a short, fixed gaming time." 
4. "Sleep and exercise come first; they help you concentrate and feel better." 
5. "If a game distracts you, try app timers or uninstalling it for a while." 
6. "I’ll help you stick to this — we can pick a hobby or exercise together."

Explanation:
The letter (a) is written in a gentle, brotherly tone: it states the problem, offers practical steps (plan, sleep, timers), suggests gradual change and offers support — all effective in motivational communication. The schedule (b) uses fixed blocks for focused study, rest and a limited evening gaming slot (45 minutes) to create structure; it prioritizes sleep and physical activity because routine improves attention and academic performance. The list of negative effects (c) highlights common impacts of excessive gaming supported by research and observation: academics, sleep, physical and social health, and time-management skills. The suggested alternatives are realistic, constructive replacements that provide social, physical, and creative benefits. The talking-points (d) are short, memorable phrases for a respectful conversation: they combine empathy, boundary-setting, practical steps and a cooperative offer to help, which increases the chance of positive behavior change. Together these parts give Jordan a clear path: understand the issue, adopt a balanced routine, replace gaming with healthy activities, and use social support to sustain the change.

Question #163 (ID: 578687)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You have been assigned to prepare a 200-word composition titled "English: A Gateway to Global Opportunities." In addition to writing the composition, you must provide a brief three-point outline, list practical advantages of learning English, and craft a strong concluding sentence that could end the piece.

Options:
a. Write the 200-word composition.
b. Give a three-point outline (Introduction, Body, Conclusion) with 1–2 sentences for each point.
c. List four practical advantages of learning English.
d. Write a strong concluding sentence suitable to end the composition.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a English: A Gateway to Global Opportunities

English connects people across continents and opens pathways to education, work, and culture. As the predominant language in international business, science, technology, and aviation, English gives learners access to vast information and professional networks. In academic settings, many textbooks, journals, and online courses are available in English, making advanced study and research more accessible. Proficiency in English also enhances employability; employers often seek candidates who can communicate with global partners and clients. Beyond careers, English facilitates travel, allowing individuals to navigate foreign environments and form friendships with people from diverse backgrounds. Digital communication and media—websites, social networks, and entertainment—are largely dominated by English, enabling users to participate in global conversations and stay informed about world events. Learning English cultivates critical thinking and confidence, as learners practice expressing ideas clearly and understanding different perspectives. It does not replace native languages but complements them, providing tools to engage on an international stage while preserving cultural identity. By investing time in English, students and professionals equip themselves with versatile skills that expand opportunities, foster cross-cultural understanding, and support lifelong learning. Thus, mastering English is an investment in personal growth and global participation that yields lasting benefits indeed.

b Outline:
1) Introduction: Define English as a global lingua franca and state its relevance in modern life (1 sentence).
2) Body: Present key roles—education, career, communication, and digital access—with short examples to show how English creates opportunities (2 sentences).
3) Conclusion: Emphasize that learning English complements native languages and empowers individuals for global engagement (1 sentence).

c Four practical advantages:
1) Access to global education and research materials (textbooks, journals, online courses).
2) Improved job prospects in multinational companies, tourism, IT, and international trade.
3) Easier international travel and cross-cultural communication.
4) Greater access to digital content, news, and professional networks.

d Strong concluding sentence:
"Mastering English equips learners with the confidence and skills to seize global opportunities while enriching their personal and professional lives."

Explanation:
Composition reasoning: The composition emphasizes the central roles of English in education, career, travel, and digital communication to mirror common real-world motivations for learning the language. It balances positive outcomes (opportunities, access) with a note that English complements—not replaces—native languages, which makes the argument culturally sensitive.

Outline reasoning: The three-point outline follows a conventional essay structure—introduce the topic, give supporting details with examples, and conclude with a summary that reinforces the main message. Each point is kept concise to match the 1–2 sentence requirement.

Advantages reasoning: The four listed advantages are practical and observable effects of English proficiency: education/research, employability, travel/communication, and digital/media access. These cover academic, economic, social, and technological domains to show broad benefits.

Concluding sentence reasoning: The chosen concluding sentence succinctly restates the main benefit (global opportunities) while highlighting personal and professional growth, providing a strong, affirmative close that ties back to the composition's themes.

Question #164 (ID: 578688)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You have been asked by your school magazine to prepare a short project on Healthy Eating Habits that includes a written composition, key benefits, a sample one-day meal plan, and practical tips for students to follow.

Options:
a. Write a composition of about 200 words on "Healthy Eating Habits".
b. List five important benefits of maintaining healthy eating habits.
c. Suggest a simple one-day balanced meal plan suitable for a student.
d. Give five practical tips to help students adopt and maintain healthy eating habits.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Answer:
Healthy Eating Habits

Healthy eating means choosing a variety of foods that provide the nutrients the body needs to function well every day. A balanced diet includes plenty of fruits and vegetables, whole grains, lean proteins, dairy or fortified alternatives, and small amounts of healthy fats. Eating regular meals and controlling portion sizes help maintain steady energy levels and prevent overeating. Hydration is also essential; water supports digestion, circulation, and temperature regulation. Reducing the intake of highly processed foods, sugary drinks, and excessive salt keeps the body protected from long-term illnesses such as obesity, diabetes, and heart disease. Besides physical benefits, healthy eating supports mental focus, improves mood, and strengthens the immune system—important for students facing study stress and activities. Planning meals, reading food labels, and preparing simple home-cooked dishes are practical ways to build good habits. Mindful eating—paying attention to hunger and fullness cues—encourages better food choices and appreciation for meals. Overall, adopting healthy eating habits is an investment in lifelong well-being: small consistent changes lead to sustained health, improved academic performance, and a higher quality of life.

b Answer:
1) Improved concentration and academic performance; 2) Stronger immune system and fewer illnesses; 3) Healthy growth and development; 4) Better weight management and lower risk of chronic diseases; 5) More stable moods and energy levels throughout the day.

c Answer:
One-day balanced meal plan for a student:
- Breakfast: Oat porridge made with milk (or fortified plant milk), topped with sliced banana and a few nuts.
- Mid-morning snack: A small apple and a handful of unsalted almonds.
- Lunch: Brown rice or whole-wheat chapati, grilled chicken or lentil curry, mixed vegetable salad, and a yogurt.
- Afternoon snack: Carrot sticks with hummus or a piece of fruit.
- Dinner: Baked fish or tofu, steamed vegetables, quinoa or whole-wheat pasta, and a small portion of salad.
- Fluids: Water throughout the day; limit sugary drinks. A cup of milk or unsweetened tea if desired.

d Answer:
1) Plan meals ahead and pack healthy snacks to avoid junk food temptation.
2) Include a fruit or vegetable at every meal to boost fiber and vitamins.
3) Practice portion control—use smaller plates and listen to fullness cues.
4) Cook simple recipes at home to control ingredients and reduce processed food intake.
5) Stay hydrated and avoid replacing meals with energy drinks or sugary beverages.

Explanation:
The composition (a) emphasizes the core elements of a healthy diet—variety, balance, regular meals, hydration, and moderation—because these are the foundation for physical and mental well-being. The benefits listed in (b) reflect physiological and cognitive outcomes supported by nutrition science: adequate macro- and micronutrients improve immune function, growth, cognition, mood, and chronic disease risk. The sample meal plan (c) follows basic principles: complex carbohydrates for steady energy, lean protein for repair and satiety, vegetables and fruits for vitamins and fiber, and healthy fats in small amounts; it is practical for a student and easy to prepare. The tips (d) are behavioral strategies that encourage consistency—planning, including produce at every meal, portion awareness, home cooking, and hydration—all shown to help form lasting healthy eating patterns. Together, these parts form a coherent project that is actionable for students: education plus simple, specific steps increases the likelihood of adopting healthier habits.

Question #165 (ID: 578689)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: You have been asked to prepare a short writing portfolio about public learning resources. The portfolio should show a clear composition and supporting details that highlight why such resources matter for students and the community.

Options:
a. Write a composition titled "Value of Libraries" in about 200 words.
b. Name three types of libraries and write one sentence describing the main purpose of each.
c. List five specific ways libraries benefit students' academic and personal development.
d. Write a single persuasive concluding sentence encouraging someone to visit a library every week.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Value of Libraries

Libraries are sanctuaries of knowledge that serve individuals and communities alike. They provide free and organized access to books, periodicals, and digital media, making learning inclusive regardless of a person's background. For students, libraries offer quiet study spaces, reference collections, and access to research materials that support coursework and foster independent inquiry. Beyond academic needs, libraries host programs—story hours, workshops, and lectures—that build literacy, critical thinking, and social skills across all ages. Modern libraries blend traditional print with technology: computers, online databases, and e-books extend learning beyond physical walls and connect users to global information. Librarians guide patrons in locating reliable sources, developing research strategies, and evaluating information critically—an essential skill in an era of abundant but uneven-quality content. Libraries also strengthen community bonds by providing meeting rooms, cultural events, and resources for job searches or civic engagement. In short, libraries cultivate curiosity, support formal education, and promote lifelong learning, making them indispensable institutions in a healthy, informed society.

b Three types of libraries

Public library: Serves the general public with free access to a broad range of books, multimedia, and community programs.

Academic library: Supports the teaching and research needs of a college or university with specialized collections, scholarly journals, and study spaces.

Special (or specialized) library: Focuses on a specific subject or organization—such as law, medicine, or a corporation—providing targeted resources and expert support.

c Five specific benefits for students

1. Access to curated research materials (books, journals, databases) that support assignments and projects.
2. Quiet, structured study environments that improve concentration and productivity.
3. Guidance from librarians on information literacy and proper citation practices.
4. Free access to computers, internet, and software for students who lack these at home.
5. Extracurricular learning opportunities—workshops, reading groups, and tutoring—that enhance skills and confidence.

d Persuasive concluding sentence

Visit your local library every week to discover new ideas, get help with learning, and connect with a community that supports your growth.

Explanation:
The composition emphasizes the multifunctional role of libraries: as repositories of books and as active community centers offering digital access, programs, and professional guidance. The structure follows a clear paragraph flow—definition, student-focused benefits, modern features (digital resources), librarian roles, community functions, and conclusion—to make the argument cohesive. The three library types are standard categories used in library science and practical descriptions highlight their differing missions. The five benefits for students combine tangible resources (materials, technology) with environmental and instructional supports (study spaces, librarian guidance, programs), covering academic and personal development. The concluding sentence is short and persuasive, aimed at habit-forming: it mixes an action (visit weekly) with promised outcomes (discover ideas, get help, connect), which is an effective rhetorical move to motivate regular engagement.

Question #170 (ID: 578684)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: In early 2025 a nationwide Student Campaign for Merit-based University Admissions emerged after a sudden policy change reduced open seats in public universities and introduced new reservation categories. Students from diverse backgrounds organized rallies, online petitions and campus strikes demanding transparency and equal opportunity. The movement drew inspiration from earlier student protests and sparked debates on merit, social justice and affirmative action.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition on "Student Campaign for Merit-based University Admissions."
b. List three immediate causes that triggered this 2025 student campaign and explain each in one sentence.
c. Recommend two non-violent tactics the students could use to sustain public support, and explain why each would be effective (one short paragraph each).
d. Propose two policy changes the government or universities could adopt to balance merit and social equity; explain how each policy addresses the students' concerns.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Composition: The Student Campaign for Merit-based University Admissions of 2025 was a vivid example of youth mobilization for educational fairness. Triggered by a rapid policy shift that reduced open merit seats and added new reservation categories without broad consultation, students across cities and campuses organized peaceful sit-ins, teach-ins and social media drives to voice their concern. The movement combined respect for merit with calls for transparent, data-driven affirmative measures for disadvantaged groups, arguing that fairness requires both opportunity and accountability. Drawing on earlier student movements, activists used nonviolent discipline, clear messaging and alliances with faculty and civil-society groups to win national attention. Media coverage highlighted personal stories of aspiring students blocked from admission and exposed opaque administrative procedures. While some demonstrations faced tense moments when provoked by outside actors, the core remained committed to dialogue. After weeks of negotiations, a joint committee of students, university administrators and independent experts was formed to review admission criteria and recommend reforms. The campaign reinforced the idea that educated youth can influence policy and that sustainable reform must combine merit-based selection with targeted, transparent support for the disadvantaged.

b Causes:
1) Sudden policy change: Authorities implemented new reservation categories and reduced open seats without stakeholder consultation, causing immediate grievance.
2) Lack of transparency: Admission criteria and quota calculations were opaque, fueling perceptions of unfairness and arbitrary decision-making.
3) Threat to upward mobility: Many students feared the policy would block talented, low-income applicants who relied on merit-based access to higher education.

c Non-violent tactics:
1) Nationwide teach-ins and public forums — By organizing educational sessions on campuses and public spaces, students can explain their demands, present evidence, and engage communities, converting bystanders into informed supporters and reducing misinformation.
2) Coordinated digital petitions and storytelling campaigns — Using verified personal stories, data visualizations and petitions amplifies reach, exerts reputational pressure on authorities, and keeps international and local media interest, all while minimizing risk of street confrontations.

d Policy recommendations:
1) Establish a transparent, independent admissions review commission — An independent body with student and expert representation would audit quotas and admission procedures, publish methodology and data, and recommend adjustments, addressing concerns about opacity and arbitrary decisions.
2) Implement targeted support programs rather than blanket seat reductions — Instead of shifting seats away from merit lists, provide remedial tuition, scholarships and preparatory programs for disadvantaged groups so equity is achieved through capacity-building while preserving merit-based entry paths.

Explanation:
Explanation: The composition (a) emphasizes narrative elements—cause, methods, alliances, and outcomes—to mirror how student movements typically unfold and to keep the piece within the requested 200-word scope. For (b), the three causes were chosen because policy change, transparency, and perceived threats to social mobility are commonly immediate triggers for student protests; each cause is concise and directly linked to grievances that mobilize students. For (c), non-violent tactics were recommended to sustain broad public sympathy and minimize escalation: teach-ins build informed consent and local support, while digital storytelling leverages modern communication channels to maintain momentum without physical risk. For (d), the two policy proposals aim to reconcile merit and equity: an independent commission addresses institutional distrust and transparency, whereas targeted support programs create pathways for disadvantaged students without reducing merit opportunities. Together the answers present practical, politically viable approaches that respond to students' demands while suggesting constructive institutional reforms.

Question #172 (ID: 578681)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: You are asked to prepare a short composition and related responses on the theme of plastic pollution, its causes, consequences, and remedies. Use the context to complete the sub-questions below.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition on "Plastic Pollution".
b. Identify and explain three major sources of plastic pollution.
c. List four ways plastic pollution harms human health and the environment.
d. Propose five practical measures individuals and governments can implement to reduce plastic pollution.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Plastic Pollution

Plastic pollution is one of the most pressing environmental problems of the twenty-first century. Single-use plastics, improperly discarded packaging, and microplastics accumulate in soils, rivers, and oceans, harming wildlife and disrupting ecosystems. Animals ingest or become entangled in plastic debris, which leads to injury, starvation, and death. Plastics also transport invasive species and toxic chemicals through food chains, ultimately affecting human health. Microplastics have been found in drinking water, seafood, and even the air we breathe. The durability that makes plastic useful also causes it to persist, breaking into smaller fragments rather than biodegrading. Tackling plastic pollution requires coordinated action at many levels: reducing production of unnecessary single-use items, improving waste collection and recycling infrastructure, and promoting alternatives made from biodegradable or reusable materials. Public education campaigns and extended producer responsibility policies can shift consumption patterns and hold manufacturers accountable. Communities should organize cleanup drives and encourage compostable packaging for organic waste. Governments must enforce regulations to limit plastic waste and support research into sustainable materials. If we change how we produce, consume, and manage plastic, we can protect ecosystems and safeguard health for current and future generations. Acting now will ensure a cleaner planet and stronger economies.

b Three major sources of plastic pollution:
1) Single-use packaging: Items like plastic bags, wrappers, and disposable bottles are produced in massive quantities and often discarded after one use, easily becoming litter that moves into waterways and landscapes.
2) Inadequate waste management: Poor collection, open dumping, and lack of recycling infrastructure cause plastics to escape disposal systems and accumulate in the environment.
3) Microplastics from fragmentation and products: Larger plastic breaks down into microplastics; additionally, microbeads from personal care products and synthetic fibers from washing clothes enter water systems directly.

c Four harms to health and environment:
1) Wildlife injury and death: Entanglement and ingestion cause choking, internal injury, and starvation for many animals.
2) Ecosystem disruption: Plastic alters habitats, transports invasive species, and affects food webs.
3) Human health risks: Microplastics and associated chemicals can enter food and water, potentially causing toxic and endocrine effects.
4) Economic and social impacts: Tourism, fisheries, and coastal communities suffer losses from polluted environments.

d Five practical measures:
1) Reduce and replace: Phase out unnecessary single-use plastics and promote reusable or biodegradable alternatives.
2) Improve waste systems: Invest in collection, sorting, and recycling infrastructure and sanitary landfills.
3) Regulatory measures: Enact bans, taxes, or extended producer responsibility policies to make producers accountable for plastic waste.
4) Public education and behavior change: Run campaigns to encourage reuse, proper disposal, and participation in cleanups.
5) Support innovation and research: Fund development of sustainable materials, improved recycling technologies, and safer product design.

Explanation:
The composition (a) is structured to introduce the problem, describe impacts, and propose broad solutions within the 200-word limit; language emphasizes persistence of plastics and the need for multi-level action. For (b), the chosen sources cover the main pathways plastics enter the environment: consumer single-use items, failures in waste systems, and microplastic generation from products and fragmentation. These are the most commonly reported contributors in environmental studies. For (c), effects are grouped into ecological (wildlife, ecosystems), human health (microplastics and chemicals), and socio-economic impacts (livelihoods and tourism) to show the multifaceted harm. For (d), suggested measures combine prevention (reduce/replace), system fixes (waste management), policy tools (regulation and producer responsibility), social strategies (education), and technological progress (innovation). Together these actions target both the supply and demand sides and the lifecycle of plastic products, reflecting best-practice recommendations from environmental science and policy. Each recommendation is practical and scalable: individuals can reduce and participate in recycling and cleanups, while governments can set rules, invest in infrastructure, and incentivize alternatives.

Sub-Questions:

Explanation:

- Offering to bring the damaged card: Helps the office confirm the claim and speeds processing.
- Formal tone and respectful language: Appropriate for communication with a school authority.

Tips: Attach or be ready to show a photo of the damaged card if available, and check the school office hours or replacement fee policy before visiting to avoid extra trips.

================================================================================
Question #182 (ID: 578670)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: Over the past year many households across Bangladesh have felt a steady rise in the price of everyday goods and services. Middle-income families in both urban and peri-urban areas report tighter budgets, cuts in savings, and difficult choices about food, health, and education. Local officials, market experts, and NGOs are discussing immediate and long-term responses to ease the burden on these families.

Options:
a. Write a composition on "Rising Cost of Living in Bangladesh and Its Effects on Middle-Income Families" in 200 words.
b. List five main causes of the rising cost of living in Bangladesh, briefly explaining each cause in one sentence.
c. Propose five practical measures the government and civil society can implement to protect middle-income families from price shocks, with one short justification for each measure.
d. Write a concise concluding remark (35–45 words) on why controlling the cost of living is essential for national development.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Rising Cost of Living in Bangladesh and Its Effects on Middle-Income Families

The rising cost of living in Bangladesh has become an urgent challenge for middle-income families who once maintained modest but stable lifestyles. Food prices, fuel, housing rents and transport fares have climbed faster than wages, forcing households to reduce savings and curtail non-essential spending. Many families cope by cutting nutritious foods, delaying medical visits, and postponing educational expenses. Small entrepreneurs and salaried workers face shrinking disposable income, which lowers domestic demand and slows local economic activity. Women often shoulder extra financial pressure, taking informal work or longer hours to supplement family income. Increased borrowing from informal lenders creates cycles of debt that are hard to escape. Social consequences include stress, deteriorating health outcomes, and a threat to children’s schooling and future prospects. Addressing this requires both short-term relief—such as targeted subsidies, stricter enforcement against hoarding, and market price monitoring—and long-term structural reforms like boosting domestic agricultural productivity, improving supply chains, and creating wage growth through skills development and job creation. Only with coordinated policy action and community support can middle-income families regain economic stability and contribute effectively to national development.

b Five main causes (one-sentence explanations):
1. Inflationary pressure: General inflation reduces purchasing power as prices rise across multiple sectors faster than incomes.
2. Supply-chain disruptions: Transport bottlenecks and higher fuel costs increase distribution expenses, which pass to consumers.
3. Import dependence: Reliance on imported food and fuel makes domestic prices vulnerable to global market volatility and exchange-rate shifts.
4. Natural shocks: Floods, floods or droughts damage crops and disrupt production, shrinking supply and driving up food prices.
5. Market malpractice: Hoarding, speculation, and weak enforcement allow unscrupulous traders to push prices up artificially.

c Five practical measures with justifications:
1. Targeted cash transfers to vulnerable middle-income households — provide immediate relief without large universal subsidies.
2. Strengthened market monitoring and anti-hoarding enforcement — deter price manipulation and stabilize supply.
3. Encourage local production and value chains (grants, cold storage, logistics) — reduce import dependence and supply volatility.
4. Fuel and transport policy reform (efficient subsidies, public transit investment) — lower distribution costs and ease household commuting expenses.
5. Skills training and wage support programs — boost household incomes through better employment opportunities to keep pace with rising costs.

d Concluding remark (40 words):
Controlling the cost of living is vital to protect household welfare, sustain consumer demand, and prevent social unrest; stable prices enable investment in health, education and businesses, which in turn supports inclusive and resilient national economic growth.

Explanation:
The composition (a) summarizes how price rises affect middle-income families, linking short-term coping strategies to broader social and economic outcomes; it balances immediate relief and long-term reform recommendations. The causes list (b) focuses on common drivers observable in Bangladesh: inflation, supply-chain problems, import reliance, climatic damage to production, and market abuse. Each cause is kept to one sentence for clarity. The proposed measures (c) mix short-term and structural interventions: targeted cash transfers and enforcement address urgent needs and market integrity, while boosting local production and investing in transport reduce future vulnerability; skills and wage support help incomes keep pace with prices. The concluding remark (d) emphasizes why controlling living costs matters for both household well-being and national development, linking price stability to social cohesion and economic resilience. Together, these answers provide a coherent analysis and practical policy direction consistent with the contextual scenario.

Question #184 (ID: 578672)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are asked to prepare materials for a school environmental week focused on clean energy. The packet should include a short composition and focused answers to help students understand the topic clearly.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition on "Renewable Energy and Sustainable Living".
b. List three major advantages of adopting renewable energy, with one-sentence explanations for each.
c. Identify three key challenges in shifting from fossil fuels to renewables, with brief explanations.
d. Recommend five practical actions an individual student can take to support sustainable living and renewable energy adoption.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Renewable Energy and Sustainable Living

Renewable energy sources—such as solar, wind, hydro, and geothermal—together with sustainable living practices, form a powerful response to the climate crisis. Adopting renewables reduces reliance on finite fossil fuels and lowers greenhouse gas emissions that drive global warming. Communities benefit from cleaner air, improved public health, and increased energy security when local and distributed generation replaces centralized polluting power plants. Sustainable living complements technology: conserving energy through efficient appliances, better insulation, and mindful consumption shrinks demand and makes renewable systems more effective. Economic gains follow as well—renewable industries create jobs in manufacturing, installation, and maintenance, while decentralized energy can stabilize costs for households. Challenges remain, including intermittency, the need for storage and smarter grids, and the upfront investment required to scale technologies equitably. Addressing these requires policy support, innovation in batteries and grid management, and public engagement. Ultimately, combining a shift to clean energy with everyday sustainable choices—reducing waste, choosing active transport, and supporting green policies—helps ensure a resilient, fair, and healthier future for all.

b Advantages:
1) Reduced greenhouse gas emissions — Renewables emit little to no CO2 during operation, cutting climate-warming pollution.
2) Energy security and diversification — Local renewable resources reduce dependence on imported fuels and price volatility.
3) Job creation and economic growth — Manufacturing, installation, and maintenance of renewable systems generate employment and local investment.

c Challenges:
1) Intermittency — Solar and wind vary with weather and time, requiring storage, demand management, or backup systems.
2) Infrastructure and cost of transition — Upgrading grids, building storage, and replacing legacy assets need substantial upfront investment and planning.
3) Policy, social and equity issues — Inadequate policies, resistance from vested interests, and unequal access can slow fair deployment.

d Five practical actions for students:
1) Conserve energy at home and school (turn off lights, use energy-efficient bulbs and appliances).
2) Advocate for and participate in school solar or green-energy projects (help start campaigns, fundraising, or installations).
3) Use low-carbon transport: walk, cycle, carpool, or use public transit when possible.
4) Reduce, reuse, recycle, and cut food waste—especially reducing high-carbon foods like excessive red meat.
5) Learn and spread awareness: organize talks, share reliable information, and encourage local leaders to support renewable-friendly policies.

Explanation:
The composition (a) summarizes why renewable energy plus sustainable living is central to addressing climate change: emissions reduction, public health, energy security, and economic benefits. The listed advantages (b) were chosen as they capture environmental, strategic, and socioeconomic gains that commonly motivate policy and personal choices. The challenges (c) highlight the technical (intermittency), economic (infrastructure cost), and social/political barriers that must be managed; each is a common, practical obstacle in energy transitions. The five student actions (d) focus on behaviors and initiatives with immediate impact and educational value: conserving energy reduces demand, school projects demonstrate feasibility, low-carbon transport cuts emissions, waste/food choices lower embedded emissions, and advocacy builds social and political momentum. Together the answers aim to provide a concise, teachable package suitable for school activities and discussion during an environmental week.

Question #185 (ID: 578664)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are the elder sister/brother of Rafi who has recently begun skipping classes, spending hours on his phone and gaming, and has started mixing with a group of classmates who encourage careless behaviour. As an elder sibling you are worried about his future. Prepare responses to the following tasks to help guide him back to discipline and study.

Options:
a. Write a personal letter to Rafi advising him to stop wasting time, avoid bad company and take his studies seriously. The letter should be warm but firm and include specific steps he can take.
b. List five concise pieces of advice (each one sentence) that Rafi can follow immediately.
c. Write a short persuasive paragraph (4–6 sentences) addressed to your parents explaining why a supportive approach will work better than punishment and suggesting one concrete way they can help Rafi.
d. Create a simple weekly study schedule for Rafi (Mon–Sun) that balances study, rest, and recreational time, suitable for a secondary-school student.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Dear Rafi,

House No. 12, Green Lane
Dhaka
15 March 2025

My dear Rafi,

I am writing because I am worried about you. Lately you have been skipping classes, spending most evenings on your phone and games, and following friends who do not care about their future. I know you are capable of much more — you have always been sharp and kind. That is why I want to remind you gently but firmly that these months matter for your future.

Please try these steps right away: set a daily study routine, put your phone away during study hours, meet friends who encourage good habits, join a school club or sports activity to channel your energy, and ask for help from teachers when you find subjects hard. Start with small goals: attend all classes for one week, finish homework on the same day, and go to bed by 10:30 pm. I will help you make a simple plan and check in with you every evening for the first two weeks.

I believe in you, Rafi. Making these changes will not only improve your marks but also give you confidence and better options later. If you ever feel pressured or stuck, talk to me — we can work through it together without blame.

With love and concern,

Your sister/brother,

Amina

b 1. Put your phone on silent and out of sight during all study periods.
2. Attend every class for at least two weeks to rebuild your routine.
3. Replace one hour of gaming with a sport or club activity each day.
4. Do today’s homework today; don’t let tasks pile up.
5. Ask one teacher for help if a topic is unclear instead of giving up.

c Dear Mom and Dad,

I ask you to consider a supportive approach for Rafi rather than harsh punishment. He is acting out from confusion and peer pressure, not from a desire to fail. If we calmly set clear expectations, help him build a simple routine, and praise small improvements, he is more likely to respond positively. I suggest we hold a short family meeting to listen to him, agree on a daily study time, and offer a small reward (like a weekend outing) for a full week of class attendance. This will show him we care and encourage lasting change.

d Weekly study schedule (sample for a secondary-school student):

Monday–Friday:
- 6:00–7:00 am: Wake up, light exercise, breakfast
- 7:30–2:30 pm: School (stay attentive; take brief notes)
- 3:30–4:30 pm: Short rest/snack + 30 minutes free time
- 4:30–6:00 pm: Focused study session (homework & revision)
- 6:00–7:00 pm: Dinner and family time
- 7:00–8:00 pm: Second study session (difficult subjects)
- 8:00–8:30 pm: Light recreation/relaxation (walk/reading)
- 8:30–9:30 pm: Quick review of the day’s lessons
- 10:30 pm: Bedtime

Saturday:
- Morning: 9:00–11:00 am — Revision of weekly topics
- Afternoon: Free time / sports / hobby
- Evening: 7:00–8:00 pm — Plan for next week

Sunday:
- Morning: 9:00–11:00 am — Practice tests or extra study for weak subjects
- Afternoon: Family time and rest
- Evening: Prepare school bag and set goals for Monday

Notes: Limit gaming to a maximum of 1 hour on weekdays (after studies) and 2 hours on weekends; phone to be used only during designated breaks. Adjust times to match school hours and extracurriculars.

Explanation:
This set of responses is designed to combine empathy with concrete actions, which research and experience show are the most effective for changing adolescent behaviour. The letter (a) uses a warm but firm tone to maintain trust while setting expectations. The short advice list (b) gives immediate, actionable steps Rafi can implement that reduce friction (phone away, attend classes, swap one hour of gaming for healthy activity). The paragraph to parents (c) recommends supportive strategies because positive reinforcement and structured support typically produce better long-term results than punishment alone. The weekly schedule (d) balances focused study blocks with breaks, exercise and sleep — essential elements for concentration and memory. Small, consistent changes (daily routines, parental support, and accountability from a sibling) are more sustainable than drastic overnight transformations.

Part (b) lists realistic, time-phased steps that build on education, experience, and professional development—important for achieving a teaching career. Question #187 (ID: 578666)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Suppose you are 'Riya', a student of IX Govt. School, Sylhet. You know how important English is for study and future life, but your younger brother Shohag, a student of class VII, feels English is difficult and does not want to try. Now prepare: a polite letter to Shohag describing the importance of learning English in our practical life, plus practical guidance to help him improve.

Options:
a. Write a letter to your younger brother Shohag explaining the importance of learning English in practical life.
b. Give five practical tips Shohag can follow every day to improve his English. Explain briefly why each tip helps.
c. List three common mistakes students make while learning English and explain how Shohag can avoid them.
d. Prepare a simple 8-week weekly plan (activities per week) Shohag can follow to improve his reading and speaking skills.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
Dear Shohag,
Sylhet, 10 August 2025

I hope you are well. I am writing because I want to tell you why learning English is important and how it can help you in real life. English is used all over the world for study, work and communicating on the internet. If you learn English well, you can read good books and websites, watch useful educational videos, understand computer instructions, and apply for better jobs in future. Many university courses and science books are written in English. When you travel or meet people from other places, English often helps you speak with them.

I know English seems difficult now, but small daily practice will make it easier. Try to read a short paragraph, speak a few simple sentences, and watch a video in English a little every day. Do not be afraid of making mistakes — everyone makes them while learning. With time you will see improvement, and it will open many doors for you in education, career and life.

Take care and start with one small step today. I believe in you.

Your loving sister,
Riya

b
1. Read one short English paragraph daily (news snippet or story): Reading improves vocabulary and grammar exposure. Even one paragraph helps you learn new words in context.

2. Speak aloud for 10 minutes every day (describe your day or retell a short story): Speaking builds fluency and confidence; vocal practice trains pronunciation and reduces fear.

3. Watch a short English video with subtitles (children’s programmes or educational clips): Listening improves comprehension and familiarizes you with natural expressions and intonation.

4. Keep a small vocabulary notebook and learn 3 new words daily with example sentences: Writing and revising words helps long-term retention and practical use.

5. Use simple English chat/apps to write messages to friends or family: Writing regularly improves structure and gives low-pressure practice to form sentences.

c
1. Mistake: Memorizing isolated words without context.
   How to avoid: Learn words with a sentence or example so you know how they are used.

2. Mistake: Focusing only on grammar rules and not using the language.
   How to avoid: Balance grammar study with speaking and listening practice. Use grammar in short speaking exercises.

3. Mistake: Avoiding speaking for fear of mistakes.
   How to avoid: Start with simple sentences, practice aloud at home, and accept mistakes as part of learning. Correct gently and keep trying.

d
8-Week Plan (weekly activities, repeat or progress each week):
Week 1: Read one short paragraph each day + speak 5 minutes aloud (introduce yourself and your daily routine).
Week 2: Read one paragraph + speak 7 minutes (describe your favourite hobby) + learn 3 new words daily.
Week 3: Read short news/children’s story + speak 10 minutes (retell the story) + watch two short English videos with subtitles that week.
Week 4: Read and write a short summary (3–5 sentences) once a week + daily speaking 10 minutes + review vocabulary notebook.
Week 5: Start a simple conversation practice twice a week with a family member or friend in English (5–10 minutes) + continue reading and vocabulary.
Week 6: Record yourself speaking a 1–2 minute paragraph and listen for pronunciation; watch one educational video and repeat sentences aloud.
Week 7: Read a slightly longer passage each week and discuss its meaning in English (5–10 minutes) + expand vocabulary to 4 words/day.
Week 8: Prepare and present a short 2–3 minute talk (topic: My school or My dream) to family; continue daily reading and speaking. After Week 8, review progress and set new targets.

Follow these activities consistently. Each week increase practice time slowly and celebrate small improvements.

Explanation:
The letter (part a) is short, polite and motivational: it explains practical uses of English (education, internet, jobs, travel) and encourages small steps. The five tips (part b) combine reading, speaking, listening, vocabulary and writing practice — these address the main language skills and are realistic for a class VII student. The common mistakes (part c) focus on typical pitfalls: learning words without context, overemphasizing rules without use, and fear of speaking; each remedy is practical and action-based. The 8-week plan (part d) gives a progressive, achievable schedule that balances reading, speaking, listening and vocabulary with gradual increases in time and complexity. Regular short practices build habit and confidence, which is more effective than occasional long study sessions.

I humbly request you to send me Tk. 1,800 as soon as possible so I can pay the hostel and get the treatment done. I promise to manage my spending carefully and will send you a full receipt of expenses.

Please pray for my success and give my love to everyone at home.

Your loving daughter,

Sima

(Studying at City College)

d Requested amount: Tk. 1,800

Breakdown:
- Hostel fee increment: Tk. 1,200
- Medical consultation and medicines: Tk. 500
- Small contingency (transport, minor supplies): Tk. 100

Explanation:
a) The subject line must be concise and clearly state the purpose so the parent immediately understands the urgency and reason for the mail. Mentioning both 'hostel fee' and 'medical expenses' signals necessity.

b) The opening sentence balances courtesy and context — it reassures the parent about your wellbeing before introducing the request. The closing sentence expresses gratitude, asks for timely help, and offers a prayer or blessing, which is culturally appropriate and respectful.

c) The full e-mail follows a standard polite structure: salutation, a brief positive opening, a clear explanation of the problem, a polite and specific request, a promise to be responsible, and an affectionate closing. Including the amount and a promise to share receipts increases credibility and makes it easier for the parent to decide.

d) Stating the exact amount and providing an itemized breakdown helps the parent understand why the money is needed. The contingency item is small and reasonable; listing it shows thoughtfulness and planning. The total is the sum of the items and is rounded to a sensible figure for quick transfer.

Question #193 (ID: 578663)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are preparing a contribution for the school magazine about the growing concern of "Smartphone Addiction." The editor asks for a short composition (~200 words) and related brief tasks to help readers understand causes, effects, and practical remedies.

Options:
a. Write a composition on "Smartphone Addiction" in about 200 words.
b. List four positive uses of smartphones that remain valuable despite the addiction problem.
c. Suggest four practical measures students can adopt to reduce smartphone addiction.
d. Write a concise 20-word summary of the composition.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Smartphone Addiction
 
 Smartphones have transformed how we communicate, learn, and access information, but their constant availability has given rise to smartphone addiction. This condition shows up as compulsive checking, excessive screen time, and difficulty concentrating on tasks without reaching for the device. Common causes include social media algorithms that reward frequent engagement, entertaining apps and games designed to capture attention, boredom, stress relief seeking, and social pressure to stay connected. The consequences affect physical health—eye strain, headaches, poor posture, and disturbed sleep—along with mental well-being such as anxiety, reduced attention span, and lowered academic performance. Relationships can also suffer when face-to-face interactions are replaced by screens. Addressing smartphone addiction requires both personal discipline and environmental changes: set daily screen-time limits, disable nonessential notifications, schedule phone-free study and family periods, and pursue offline hobbies or exercise. Schools and parents should teach digital literacy and model balanced phone use. Occasional digital detoxes help reset habits. Ultimately, smartphones are powerful tools that can enhance life when used intentionally; guarding against addictive patterns helps preserve health, focus, and meaningful human connections.

b Four positive uses of smartphones:
 1. Instant communication with family and emergency contacts.
 2. Access to educational resources, online courses, and research.
 3. Navigation (GPS), health apps, and organizational tools (calendars, reminders).
 4. Tools for creativity and productivity (note-taking, photography, document editing).

c Four practical measures to reduce smartphone addiction:
 1. Set specific daily screen-time limits and use built-in screen-time trackers or app blockers.
 2. Turn off nonessential notifications and remove distracting apps from the home screen.
 3. Create phone-free zones/times (during meals, study hours, and before bedtime) and keep the phone physically away while working.
 4. Replace smartphone use with scheduled offline activities—reading, sports, clubs, or hobbies—and practice short digital detoxes regularly.

d 20-word summary:
 Smartphone addiction damages health, focus, and social life; disciplined use, boundaries, and digital breaks restore balance and retain benefits safely.

Explanation:
The composition (a) is structured to introduce the issue, explain causes, describe effects, and offer remedies—this mirrors a typical short essay format for a school magazine. I emphasized causes like algorithms and social pressure because they explain why addiction is widespread. The effects cover physical, mental, academic, and social domains to show multi-faceted impact. Remedies combine individual actions (limits, notification control, hobbies) with social/environmental supports (parental guidance, school policies) because sustainable change requires both. For (b) I listed four clear, constructive uses of smartphones to acknowledge they remain valuable tools. For (c) the measures are practical, easy to implement, and evidence-based (screen limits, app blockers, phone-free periods, activity substitution). For (d) I crafted a 20-word summary that captures the main message: addiction harms, but mindful habits preserve benefits. The composition is approximately 200 words to match the editor's request; the rest of the answers are concise to fit a short-format magazine feature.

In (d) the practical request is small and specific (food items that aid recovery) and the reassurance request addresses the emotional need of parents. Overall, the message balances factual health information, adherence to medical advice, and family considerations: clear subject, polite greeting, simple plain language, and a warm closing—elements that make an effective health-update e-mail to a parent.
