Question #197 (ID: 578654)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are asked to prepare a short school assignment on the topic of Child Labour in Bangladesh. The assignment should include a focused composition, practical policy ideas, a memorable slogan for a school campaign, and references to active organizations that work on this issue in the country. Use clear, age-appropriate language suitable for secondary-school students.

Options:
a. Write a composition of about 180–220 words on 'Child Labour in Bangladesh', covering causes, effects, and a brief call to action.
b. List and explain five realistic measures the government and communities can take to reduce child labour in Bangladesh.
c. Create a concise slogan (no more than 10 words) suitable for a school poster against child labour.
d. Name three organizations or institutions in Bangladesh that work on child protection or child labour issues, and give one short sentence about the role of each.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Child Labour in Bangladesh
Child labour remains a deep-rooted social problem in Bangladesh. Economic hardship, seasonal shocks, and insufficient social safety nets force many families to rely on the earnings of their children. As a result, children work in garment factories, brickfields, tea gardens, small workshops, road-side stalls and as domestic helpers. The causes are complex: persistent poverty, limited access to quality education, household debt, and employer demand for cheap, compliant labour. The effects are deeply harmful—working children are deprived of schooling, they face health risks from hazardous tasks, and many suffer physical and psychological abuse. This cycle traps families in intergenerational poverty and undermines national development by producing an unskilled workforce. To break the cycle, Bangladesh needs stricter enforcement of child-labour laws, expanded access to free, quality schooling, and targeted poverty-alleviation programs that support families so they do not need to send children to work. NGOs, community leaders and responsible businesses must join government efforts to inspect workplaces, improve wages for adults, and raise public awareness. Every child has the right to education, safety, and a healthy childhood—ending child labour is essential for a fairer and more prosperous Bangladesh.

b Five realistic measures to reduce child labour
1. Strengthen enforcement and inspections: Increase labour inspections, impose penalties for violations, and target informal workplaces where children commonly work. Regular inspections combined with a transparent reporting mechanism deter employers from hiring children.
2. Expand access to quality education: Provide free primary and secondary schooling, reduce indirect costs (uniforms, supplies), and offer flexible school hours or bridge programs for working children to re-enter education.
3. Conditional cash transfers and social protection: Give cash support or food subsidies to poor families conditional on children attending school, reducing immediate economic pressure to send children to work.
4. Livelihood and skill development for adults: Implement vocational training, microcredit and employment programs for parents so households can earn adequate income without relying on child earnings.
5. Public awareness and community mobilization: Run local campaigns, involve religious and community leaders, and set up child protection committees to change social norms and report exploitation.

c Slogan
"Education, not labour: protect every child's future."

d Three organizations in Bangladesh
1. BRAC — Implements education, child protection and livelihood programs that help prevent child labour by supporting families and offering alternative schooling.  
2. Save the Children Bangladesh — Works on child rights, protection, and education initiatives, including programs to reduce child labour and rehabilitate working children.  
3. Department of Labour (Ministry of Labour and Employment) — Government body responsible for enforcing labour laws, inspections and policy measures related to child labour.

Explanation:
Reasoning and concepts behind the solution:

Composition (a): The composition frames child labour as a multifaceted problem—linking root causes (poverty, lack of education, demand for cheap labour) to consequences (health risks, lost schooling, intergenerational poverty). It also stresses combined responsibility: government enforcement, social protection, schooling, NGOs and businesses. This structure (causes, effects, solutions, call to action) makes the piece clear and persuasive for a school assignment.

Measures (b): Each suggested measure targets a different part of the problem. Enforcement addresses supply-side illegality; education and conditional cash transfers address demand-side and household incentives; adult livelihoods reduce economic necessity; and awareness changes social norms. Together these are complementary and realistic for Bangladesh’s context.

Slogan (c): The slogan is short, memorable and positive—contrasting education with labour and emphasizing protection and the future, suitable for posters and school campaigns.

Organizations (d): BRAC and Save the Children are major NGOs active in education and child protection in Bangladesh; the Department of Labour is the governmental authority that sets and enforces legal standards. Mentioning both NGOs and government highlights the need for multi-stakeholder action.

Language and tone: All sections use simple, age-appropriate language for secondary-school students and focus on practical, implementable ideas rather than abstract theory.

Question #200 (ID: 578658)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are preparing materials for a school road safety awareness campaign. Prepare the required items below to be used in posters, classroom talks, and community outreach.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition titled 'Keeping Our Roads Safe'.
b. List five common causes of road accidents and give one practical preventive measure for each.
c. Draft a 30-word speech for students urging them to practice road safety.
d. Create three short catchy slogans (each no more than 7 words) to print on posters.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Keeping Our Roads Safe

Road safety concerns every member of our community. Every day people travel by foot, bicycle, motorcycle, bus or car; simple precautions and responsible behavior can prevent many needless tragedies. Frequent causes of accidents include speeding, distracted driving, driving under the influence, poor vehicle maintenance and unsafe road infrastructure. Pedestrians and cyclists are particularly vulnerable when roads lack sidewalks, crossings and adequate lighting.

Awareness must start early. Schools and families should teach children to look both ways before crossing, use zebra crossings, wear helmets and seatbelts, and obey traffic signs. Drivers should avoid mobile phones, respect speed limits, never drive impaired and ensure their vehicles are roadworthy. Local authorities must invest in safer road design, clear signage, pedestrian crossings, proper lighting and consistent enforcement of traffic laws. Community campaigns, practical demonstrations and regular safety drills reinforce safe habits.

Road safety saves lives and reduces emotional and financial burdens on families. When individuals adopt safe practices and authorities build and maintain safe roads, accidents will fall. Let us all commit to following rules, protecting the vulnerable and making our streets safe for everyone.

b 1) Speeding — Preventive measure: Enforce and respect speed limits; install speed bumps and clear signage in school and residential zones.
2) Distracted driving (e.g., mobile phone use) — Preventive measure: Promote hands-free policies, public education, and strict fines for phone use while driving.
3) Driving under the influence — Preventive measure: Strengthen DUI checks, provide public awareness campaigns about risks, and offer safe-ride options.
4) Poor vehicle maintenance — Preventive measure: Mandatory periodic vehicle inspections and driver education on basic upkeep (brakes, tires, lights).
5) Unsafe road infrastructure (poor lighting, lack of crossings) — Preventive measure: Improve road design with sidewalks, streetlights, zebra crossings and proper signage.

c Dear friends, road safety saves lives. Always wear helmets and seatbelts, follow signals, avoid phones while driving, respect speed limits. Protect yourself and others—practice responsibility every time you travel daily.

d 1) Slow Down, Save Lives
2) Buckle Up — Arrive Alive
3) Helmet On, Life On

Explanation:
Part a: The composition emphasizes causes, preventive actions for individuals and authorities, and a call to collective responsibility. It is structured with an introduction, body (causes and measures) and conclusion to suit a 200-word campaign piece. Part b: Each listed cause pairs directly with a practical, implementable preventive measure — enforcement, education, engineering (road design) and vehicle checks — reflecting the widely used 'three E's' of road safety: education, enforcement and engineering. Part c: The 30-word speech is concise, motivational and instructive for students: it mentions key actions (helmets, seatbelts, signals, no phones, speed) and ends with a collective responsibility message. Part d: Slogans are short, memorable and action-oriented, suitable for posters and banners; they focus on speed reduction, seatbelt use and helmet use — three high-impact behaviours that reduce injuries and fatalities.

15/A Khatun Road

Question #206 (ID: 578639)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: The internet shapes how we learn, work, socialize and govern. Consider its powerful advantages and the new social, ethical and personal challenges it creates. Prepare a short composition and related analyses that explore how individuals and families can enjoy the internet's benefits while reducing harms.

Options:
a. Write a composition titled "Digital Citizenship: Balancing Benefits and Risks of the Internet" in about 200 words.
b. List five positive impacts of the internet on education and daily life—each described in one sentence.
c. Identify five common abuses or harms associated with internet use and give one practical preventive measure for each (one sentence each).
d. Give three clear, actionable tips for parents to manage their children's internet use (one short sentence each).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Digital Citizenship: Balancing Benefits and Risks of the Internet

The internet is a transformative tool that connects people, information and services across the globe. In education it offers instant access to lectures, research and interactive learning platforms; in work it enables remote collaboration and new business models; in everyday life it simplifies shopping, banking and communication. Yet these conveniences come with responsibilities. Misinformation spreads quickly, privacy can be compromised, and excessive screen time affects mental and physical health. Responsible digital citizens verify sources, protect personal data, and balance online and offline activities. Schools and parents should teach critical thinking, digital etiquette and basic cybersecurity habits. Governments and platforms must enforce privacy standards, combat cybercrime and support digital literacy programs. When used thoughtfully, the internet amplifies creativity, broadens opportunity and strengthens communities; when used carelessly, it can isolate, mislead and harm. Striking a balance—by combining education, sensible rules and technology safeguards—allows individuals and societies to harness the web’s power while minimizing its risks, ensuring the internet remains a force for learning, connection and progress.

b Positive impacts:
1. Immediate access to vast educational resources enables self-paced learning and supports formal schooling.
2. Video calls and messaging let families and colleagues stay connected across distance.
3. Online services make everyday tasks like banking, shopping and appointments faster and more convenient.
4. Remote work and freelancing platforms create flexible job opportunities and global markets.
5. Health information and telemedicine improve access to medical advice and support in underserved areas.

c Abuses/harms and preventive measures:
1. Misinformation—verify facts with reputable sources before sharing.
2. Privacy breaches—use strong passwords, two-factor authentication and review privacy settings.
3. Cyberbullying—report abusive behavior, block offenders and keep communication records.
4. Addiction/excessive screen time—set daily limits and schedule regular offline activities.
5. Financial scams—avoid unsolicited links, confirm identities and use secure payment methods.

d Tips for parents:
1. Establish clear screen-time rules and model balanced device use yourself.
2. Use parental controls and privacy settings while discussing why they matter.
3. Encourage open conversations so children feel safe reporting online problems.

Explanation:
The composition (a) is structured to introduce both benefits and risks, then recommend education, rules and technological safeguards—this mirrors common persuasive composition formats and keeps the message balanced. The five positive impacts (b) were chosen to cover education, communication, daily convenience, employment and health to show breadth of benefit. The five harms (c) focus on common, high-impact issues—misinformation, privacy, bullying, addiction and scams—each paired with a simple, practical preventive measure to make the advice actionable. The three parental tips (d) are concise and prioritized: rule-setting and role-modeling, technical tools plus education, and open communication; together these reduce risk while preserving children’s access to learning. Word choice aimed for clarity and relevance to contemporary digital life; the composition was kept near 200 words to fulfill the prompt and to demonstrate concise, effective writing.

Question #208 (ID: 578641)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: You are asked to create a short creative composition and supporting pieces about the Victory Day of Bangladesh. Use historical facts, describe customs, write a short speech opening, and draw civic lessons. Present your responses as four parts below.

Options:
a. Write a composition (180–200 words) titled 'Reflection on Victory Day'.
b. List and briefly describe five customary ways Bangladesh commemorates Victory Day.
c. Compose a 6–8 sentence opening paragraph for a speech delivered at a Victory Day program.
d. Give three lessons modern citizens should learn from the Liberation War, and write one concise concluding sentence suitable to end the composition.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Reflection on Victory Day

December 16 stands as a luminous landmark in the story of Bangladesh: Victory Day. In 1971, after months of relentless struggle, sacrifice, and the collective yearning for freedom, the nation at last emerged independent. That victory was not merely a military success; it embodied the will of a people determined to preserve their language, culture, and dignity. Each year the country pauses to remember those who gave their lives and to honour the veterans whose courage secured our sovereignty. On this day we visit monuments, listen to eyewitness accounts, and pass on memories to younger generations so that the price of freedom remains clear. Schools hold cultural programs, hymns and patriotic songs fill the air, and the tricolour flutters from countless rooftops. Yet beyond ceremony, Victory Day challenges us to translate past heroism into present responsibility: to build just institutions, uphold human rights, and work for social progress. By doing so we keep the spirit of 1971 alive—not as nostalgia, but as inspiration for a fairer, stronger Bangladesh.

b 1) Flag hoisting and salutes: The national flag is raised across government buildings and institutions, followed by military salutes. 2) Wreath-laying at memorials: Leaders and citizens place wreaths at the National Martyrs' Memorial to honour the fallen. 3) Cultural programs and concerts: Schools, community centres, and TV channels stage songs, dramas, and recitations celebrating freedom. 4) Air and ground parades: Military and civic parades display discipline and commemorate victory. 5) Media retrospectives and documentaries: Newspapers, radio, and TV broadcast stories, interviews, and films about the Liberation War.

c Respected guests, veterans, teachers, students and dear countrymen — today we gather beneath our proud flag to remember a day that shaped our destiny. Fifty years ago our fathers and mothers, with courage and conviction, transformed sorrow into triumph and oppression into independence. We stand on their shoulders, inheriting not only land but also a responsibility to honour their sacrifice through integrity and service. Let us listen to their stories, learn from their courage, and vow to protect the ideals for which they fought. As we recall the trials of 1971, we must also renew our commitment to unity, justice and progress. May this program remind us that freedom demands vigilance, compassion and hard work from every citizen.

d Lessons for citizens: 1) Cherish and protect democratic rights: The Liberation War teaches that freedom and civil liberties are precious and must be defended. 2) Value unity and solidarity: Collective effort across communities was vital for victory and remains essential for national development. 3) Reject injustice and intolerance: The past shows the catastrophic consequences of discrimination; building an inclusive society prevents repetition. Concluding sentence: Let us honour the martyrs most truly by turning their sacrifice into daily acts of honesty, service and devotion to the nation.

Explanation:
Explanation:

Part (a) — The composition combines factual history (1971 Liberation War and December 16 surrender) with reflective commentary about remembrance and civic duty. It balances description of public observances with a forward-looking call to translate historical sacrifice into present responsibilities.

Part (b) — The five customary practices selected are common, observable elements of Victory Day commemoration that cover ceremonial, cultural, military and media aspects. Each brief description explains the purpose: remembrance, honour, education, display of national pride, and public awareness.

Part (c) — The speech opening uses formal address, invokes historical memory, acknowledges veterans, and outlines themes (unity, justice, responsibility). It follows a clear structure: greeting, historical reminder, moral obligation, call to learn, and a pledge — suitable for a public assembly.

Part (d) — The three lessons are distilled from the causes and consequences of the Liberation War: protecting rights, fostering unity, and opposing injustice. The concluding sentence is crafted to be memorable and actionable, tying commemoration to everyday civic behavior.

Overall reasoning: Each sub-part aims to be concise, accurate, and appropriate for school or community settings while encouraging reflection and constructive civic attitudes. The language is respectful, informative, and designed for a general audience.

Question:
You are spending two months on a study trip abroad and need to notify your close friend back home about your temporary whereabouts and how to contact you. Prepare the necessary communications and details so your friend can write or send small items if needed.

Options:
a. Draft an e-mail to your friend informing them of your temporary overseas address, travel reason, and how long you'll be away. Keep the tone friendly and include a clear subject line.
b. Write a concise postal address block (name and address) formatted for a postcard that your friend can use to send mail to you abroad.
c. List three small, practical items your friend could send by post to you, and explain briefly why each would be useful during your trip.
d. Compose a polite closing paragraph asking your friend to write back and suggesting one topic you would like them to include in their reply.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a To: jessica@example.com

Subject: My Temporary Address Abroad — Study Trip (May–June)

Hi Jessica,

I hope you’re doing well! I wanted to let you know I’m on a two-month study trip in Lisbon for a summer research program. I arrived on May 3 and will be here until the end of June. My temporary address while I’m here is below in case you want to write or send anything small.

I’m attending morning seminars and spending afternoons at the library and language classes — it’s been busy but exciting. I miss our coffee chats and can’t wait to tell you about the places I discover.

Temporary Address:
[See postcard block in part (b)]

Please don’t worry about sending anything bulky — just a note would make my day. Write back when you can!

Much love,
Alex

b Alex Morgan
Apt. 4B, Residência Nova
Rua das Flores 23
1250-096 Lisboa
Portugal

c 1) A small pack of original tea bags (e.g., English Breakfast) — Familiar tea can be comforting in a different place and is lightweight and allowed in most postal services.

2) A slim, printed notebook (pocket-sized) — Useful for quick notes, addresses, or sketches during the trip; compact and easy to carry.

3) A prepaid international calling card or a small rechargeable power bank (compact) — A calling card helps if local SIM or data are limited; a small power bank ensures my phone stays charged while exploring.

d Closing paragraph for the e-mail:

Please write back when you have a moment — tell me how things are at home, how Mum’s garden is doing, and any news from the neighbourhood. Your letters always brighten my days abroad. Looking forward to your updates!

Warmly,
Alex

Explanation:
Part (a) uses a friendly, personal tone appropriate for a close friend, includes subject line, reason for travel, dates, and a brief description of activities so the friend knows what to expect. It mentions the temporary address will be given (and references part b) to keep the message concise.

Part (b) presents the address in a standard, internationally legible format: recipient name, apartment/house name and number, street name and number, postal code and city, then country. This order reduces delivery confusion for international mail carriers.

Part (c) suggests items that are small, permitted by postal rules, and genuinely useful: tea for comfort, a pocket notebook for on-the-go notes, and a power-related item to support connectivity. Each item is justified in terms of practicality, size, and likelihood of passing customs.

Part (d) provides a polite, warm closing that requests a reply and gives a specific topic (the mother’s garden) to make it easier for the friend to respond. A specific prompt increases the chance of a meaningful reply. Overall, the responses balance friendliness, clarity, and practical considerations for international correspondence.

b. Write an appropriate subject line for the email.
c. Write one sentence promising how you will make up the missed classwork/homework.
d. Provide a polite closing and signature block for the email.

Solution:
a To: classteacher@your-school.edu

Subject: Request for One-Day Leave (10 September 2025)

Dear Sir/Madam,

I hope you are well. I am writing to request leave for one day on 10 September 2025 as I need to attend my cousin's wedding in another town. I will return to school on 11 September 2025.

I assure you that I will collect the class notes from my classmates and complete any missed assignments promptly.

Thanking you,

Rashed Khan
Class 7, Roll: 12
Contact: 017XXXXXXXX

b Request for One-Day Leave (10 September 2025)

c I assure you that I will collect the class notes from my classmates and submit any pending homework by 12 September 2025.

d Thanking you,

Rashed Khan
Class 7, Roll: 12
Phone: 017XXXXXXXX
Email: rashed.khan@email.com

Explanation:
This task asks for a short formal leave email and its components. Key points:

- Subject line: Should be concise and include the purpose and date so the teacher can immediately see the request (e.g., "Request for One-Day Leave (10 September 2025)").

Question #214 (ID: 578636)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: Schools and communities are planning to promote learning environments where children with disabilities study alongside their peers. The goal is to draft a short composition, identify benefits, suggest practical steps, and write a brief call to action that can be shared with teachers and parents.

Options:
a. Write a composition on "Inclusive Education for Children with Disabilities" in 200 words.
b. List three major benefits of inclusive education for students with disabilities and for their peers.
c. Name four practical measures schools can implement immediately to make classrooms more inclusive.
d. Write a concise two-sentence call to action encouraging schools and families to support inclusion.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Inclusive Education for Children with Disabilities

Inclusive education means creating classrooms where children with disabilities learn alongside their peers with the supports they need to participate fully. It begins with the belief that diversity is a strength and that every child has the right to quality schooling. Practical steps include adapting curricula, providing assistive technologies, and preparing teachers to use flexible teaching methods. Physical accessibility—ramps, wide doorways, accessible toilets—and safe transport ensure children can attend school. Individualized supports such as classroom aides, differentiated tasks, and modified assessments allow students to learn at their own pace and demonstrate their abilities. Inclusive classrooms also teach empathy, collaboration, and problem-solving to all students, helping to reduce stigma and bullying. Families, educators, and local communities must work together, backed by clear policies and funding, to sustain inclusion. When schools invest in training, resources, and an inclusive school culture, children with disabilities gain confidence and skills while the whole school benefits from richer interactions and better social outcomes. Inclusive education is not only an obligation but a path to fairer, stronger communities where no child is left behind.

b 1) Social belonging and self-esteem: Students with disabilities feel accepted, reducing isolation and improving mental health; peers learn empathy and respect.
2) Better academic and life outcomes: With appropriate supports, students with disabilities achieve higher attendance, lower dropout rates, and improved skills; peers benefit from collaborative learning.
3) Long-term economic and civic benefits: Inclusive education increases future employment prospects and civic participation, creating a more equitable and productive society.

c 1) Improve physical accessibility: ramps, accessible toilets, clear signage, and safe routes to school.
2) Teacher training and collaborative planning: basic inclusive-teaching workshops, co-teaching models, and time for planning individualized supports.
3) Provide low-cost assistive tools and adaptable materials: large-print books, slanted desks, visual schedules, and simple communication aids.
4) Implement Individualized Education Plans (IEPs) and peer-support systems: set clear, achievable goals and pair students for cooperative learning and mentoring.

d Every child deserves a safe, welcoming classroom where their abilities are recognized and supported; invest in training, accessible facilities, and simple supports today so all students can learn together. Join teachers, families, and community leaders to make inclusion the standard—because when schools include everyone, society grows stronger.

Explanation:
The composition (a) outlines the concept, practical actions, and the rationale for inclusive education, aiming for roughly 200 words to be suitable for school publications. The benefits (b) summarize social, academic, and long-term economic advantages backed by research showing inclusion reduces dropout rates and improves well-being. The practical measures (c) are chosen because they can be implemented relatively quickly and at various cost levels: physical accessibility removes basic attendance barriers; teacher training changes classroom practice; low-cost assistive tools make day-to-day learning possible; and IEPs plus peer support ensure individualized progress and social integration. The call to action (d) is concise to be usable on posters, newsletters, or speeches and stresses immediate steps and collective responsibility. Together, these parts form a coherent, actionable plan: policy and resources create the framework, while classroom practices and community commitment make inclusion real for children with disabilities and their peers.

Question #216 (ID: 578631)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
A national youth forum has been organized at your school to encourage students to think about their contribution to the country's future. The forum invites participants to prepare a short composition and answer specific tasks that reflect how young people can drive sustainable national progress.

Options:
a. Write a composition titled "Youth and Sustainable National Progress" in about 200 words.
b. Name five concrete ways in which young people can boost the nation's economy (brief points).
c. Identify three major obstacles that prevent youth from participating fully in national development and propose one practical solution for each obstacle.
d. Write a concluding paragraph (50-60 words) on the role of education in empowering youth to contribute effectively to national development.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Youth and Sustainable National Progress

Youth are the architects of tomorrow’s society. Their energy, creativity, and adaptability make them ideal agents for pursuing sustainable national progress. In the modern world, sustainable progress means balancing economic growth with social equity and environmental protection. Young people contribute by adopting green technologies, launching socially responsible enterprises, and promoting community-driven initiatives that prioritize long-term benefits over short-term gains. Education equips them with critical thinking and skills; civic engagement channels their voices into policy and governance. When supported with access to finance, mentorship, and digital infrastructure, youth-led startups can generate jobs and introduce innovations in agriculture, health, and clean energy. Moreover, youth movements raise awareness about issues like climate change, gender equality, and public health, mobilizing volunteers and creating grassroots solutions. To sustain these contributions, governments and institutions must remove barriers such as unequal education, limited funding, and political exclusion. By fostering an enabling environment—through vocational training, seed grants, and inclusive platforms—societies can convert youthful potential into measurable progress. Ultimately, a nation that invests in its youth secures resilient economic development, social cohesion, and a healthier environment for generations to come.

b Five concrete ways youth can boost the nation's economy:
1. Launching startups and small businesses that create jobs and stimulate local markets.
2. Adopting and developing digital skills (IT, freelancing, e-commerce) to earn foreign exchange.
3. Modernizing agriculture with tech-driven methods to increase productivity and supply chains.
4. Participating in vocational trades and manufacturing to strengthen domestic industries.
5. Promoting social enterprises that address community needs and reduce public expenditure.

c Three obstacles and practical solutions:
1. Obstacle: Limited access to finance for young entrepreneurs. Solution: Establish microloan programs and youth-focused seed funds with simplified application processes.
2. Obstacle: Skill mismatch between education and job market. Solution: Create industry-linked vocational training and apprenticeship schemes tied to labor demand.
3. Obstacle: Political and social exclusion of youth voices. Solution: Institute youth advisory councils in local and national bodies and guarantee youth representation in decision-making forums.

d Concluding paragraph on education (50-60 words):
Education empowers youth by providing knowledge, skills, and critical thinking needed for innovation and responsible citizenship. Quality and inclusive education bridges inequality, enhances employability, and fosters ethical leadership. By aligning curricula with real-world needs and promoting lifelong learning, education transforms young potential into practical contributions that drive sustainable national development.

Explanation:
The composition (a) emphasizes how youth contributions link to sustainable development—economic, social, and environmental dimensions—and why institutional support matters. For (b), the five ways were chosen to cover entrepreneurship, digital economy, agriculture, manufacturing, and social enterprise, representing diverse economic levers. In (c), each obstacle is common across many countries; solutions are practical, scalable interventions that governments, NGOs, or private sectors can implement to remove barriers. The concluding paragraph (d) focuses on education because skills and critical thinking are foundational for youth to participate effectively; it stays within the 50–60 word range and highlights alignment of education with labor market and civic needs.

Question #217 (ID: 578632)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Imagine a school planning to shift to a blended model where traditional classes are combined with online learning tools. The school wants a short composition and related tasks to guide teachers and parents about the benefits, practical strategies, and considerations of this shift.

Options:
a. Write a composition titled "Digital Classrooms and Student Engagement" in about 200 words.
b. List three concrete ways digital classrooms can boost student engagement, with one-sentence explanations for each.
c. Name two likely challenges the school might face during this transition and propose one practical solution for each.
d. Provide a single concluding sentence that summarizes the overall value of blending digital tools with traditional teaching.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Digital Classrooms and Student Engagement

Digital classrooms—built around learning management systems, interactive whiteboards, multimedia resources, and synchronous video—have transformed how students connect with learning. By integrating short videos, simulations, quizzes, and collaborative documents, teachers can present concepts in multiple formats that suit different learning styles. Interactive features such as live polls, breakout discussions, and gamified tasks invite students to participate actively rather than passively absorb information. Adaptive platforms and instant-feedback tools help learners identify gaps and practice targeted skills at their own pace, improving confidence and mastery. Collaboration tools extend peer interaction beyond the school day, encouraging project-based learning and peer review. For teachers, digital tools simplify tracking progress, differentiating instruction, and reusing high-quality resources. However, schools must manage screen time, ensure equitable device and internet access, and set clear expectations to minimize distractions. When thoughtfully combined with hands-on activities and face-to-face guidance, digital classrooms deepen understanding, sustain motivation, and equip students with the digital literacy needed for the future.

b 1) Interactive formative assessment: Short quizzes and live polls provide immediate feedback, keeping students accountable and helping teachers adapt lessons in real time.
2) Multimedia explanations: Videos, simulations, and animations make abstract ideas concrete and cater to visual and auditory learners, increasing comprehension and interest.
3) Collaborative tools: Shared documents and discussion platforms enable peer interaction and group projects, fostering communication skills and active participation.

c Challenge 1: Digital divide—some students lack reliable devices or internet. Solution: Provide loaner devices, create offline-accessible materials, and partner with local libraries/internet providers to expand access.
Challenge 2: Distraction and reduced focus during online activities. Solution: Establish clear digital classroom norms, use short interactive segments, alternate with offline tasks, and teach self-regulation strategies.

d Thoughtfully blended digital and traditional teaching enriches learning by increasing engagement, personalizing instruction, and preparing students for a connected world.

Explanation:
The composition (a) emphasizes multiple modalities, interactivity, and formative feedback because research and classroom practice show these features increase engagement and learning retention. The three engagement methods in (b) map to proven instructional strategies: formative assessment promotes retrieval practice and timely corrections; multimedia aligns with Cognitive Theory of Multimedia Learning by Mayer; collaboration supports social constructivist approaches. The challenges in (c) reflect common implementation barriers—accessibility and attention—so suggested solutions are practical: device loan programs, offline resources, and clear routines which have been effective in many districts. The concluding sentence (d) synthesizes the goal of blending—leveraging the strengths of both digital and in-person instruction to improve outcomes and readiness for future demands.

Question #218 (ID: 578633)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You took an overnight train to visit a seaside town with close family. The trip began at sunset and ended at dawn. Along the way you watched the countryside, shared snacks with strangers, and felt the gentle sway of the sleeper car. Use this scenario to respond to the sub-questions below.

Options:
a. Write a composition titled "A Night Train to the Coast" in about 200 words.
b. Give a brief five-point outline used to organize the composition.
c. List three sensory details (sight, sound, smell) you included and explain why each strengthens the narrative.
d. Provide an alternative title and a single concluding sentence that reflects the mood of the journey.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a A Night Train to the Coast

The night train eased out of the city as the sun tipped below the horizon, painting the sky in streaks of orange and violet. I settled into the lower berth with my small bag and watched lights blur into silhouettes. The carriage hummed with quiet conversations and the steady rhythm of wheels on rails. Outside, fields and sleeping villages slid by like pages in a slow book. A vendor passed through with tea and warm rolls; the steam and sugar mixed with the metallic tang of the carriage air. I shared my packet of biscuits with an elderly man who told me about seaside storms he had seen long ago. Midnight came and went; the gentle sway of the train lulled a few passengers to sleep while others whispered secrets under dim lights. At dawn, gulls appeared ahead, and a cool scent of salt eased into the windows. The coastline emerged, silver and calm, as the first pale light turned the sea to glass. We stepped onto the platform with sand in our shoes and tired, happy faces—ready for a day where the sky, the waves, and the memory of the journey would linger.

b Brief outline
1. Opening scene: departure at sunset and setting the mood.
2. Description of carriage life: passengers, vendor, and rhythmic motion.
3. Personal interaction: sharing food and a short conversation with a fellow traveler.
4. Nighttime atmosphere: sleep, whispers, and reflective moments.
5. Arrival at dawn: sensory arrival at the coast and concluding reflection.

c Three sensory details and why they strengthen the narrative
1. Sight — "sky in streaks of orange and violet": establishes time (sunset), creates vivid imagery, and sets an evocative tone.
2. Sound — "steady rhythm of wheels on rails": provides a grounding auditory motif that conveys motion and comfort, helping readers feel the train's movement.
3. Smell — "cool scent of salt eased into the windows": signals arrival at the coast and evokes memory and atmosphere, tying the journey to its destination.

d Alternative title and concluding sentence
Alternative title: "Moonlight Tracks to the Shore"
Concluding sentence: "We stepped onto the platform as dawn washed the sea in gentle light, carrying the hush of the night train with us into the bright day."

Explanation:
The composition follows a classic narrative arc: setting the scene, developing atmosphere, introducing a human element, and concluding with arrival and reflection. The five-point outline maps directly to paragraphs to keep the essay focused and cohesive. Sensory details were chosen to anchor the reader in moment-to-moment experience: visual imagery locates time and mood, the repetitive sound of the wheels becomes an emotional anchor, and the smell of salt signals the transition from inland to coast. The alternative title emphasizes the nocturnal and lyrical quality of the trip, while the concluding sentence aims to preserve the lingering sense of calm and continuity between the journey and the destination.

Question #219 (ID: 578634)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You have been asked to prepare a 200-word composition about the Independence Day of Bangladesh that covers its meaning, key historical events, common forms of celebration, and the lessons we should take from it. Address the four parts below in sequence.

Options:
a. Write a concise introduction (about 40–50 words) stating the date and overall significance of Independence Day.
b. Describe the main historical events (about 60–70 words) that led to the independence of Bangladesh in 1971.
c. Explain how people commonly observe and celebrate the day (about 50–60 words), mentioning at least three specific activities.
d. Conclude with the lessons and a call to action (about 30–40 words) that highlights how citizens should honor the legacy of 1971.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a The Independence Day of Bangladesh is observed on 26 March each year. It commemorates the formal proclamation of independence in 1971 and the start of the Liberation War against military oppression. The day honors the courage and sacrifices of those who fought for national sovereignty and reminds citizens of the value of freedom and self-determination.

b In late March 1971, following political breakdown and repression, the Pakistani military launched Operation Searchlight (25–26 March), resulting in mass civilian casualties. In response, Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujibur Rahman declared independence on 26 March. A nine-month Liberation War ensued, involving resistance by freedom fighters and eventual military intervention by India. The conflict ended with victory and the surrender of Pakistani forces on 16 December 1971, leading to the birth of Bangladesh.

c Observances begin with flag-hoisting and official ceremonies at the National Martyrs' Memorial, where people lay wreaths and offer prayers. Schools and cultural organizations hold rallies, songs, poems and stage performances. Television and newspapers run special programmes and documentaries. Citizens visit memorials, participate in community events, and teach younger generations about the sacrifices of 1971.

d Independence Day teaches unity, bravery and respect for human rights. To honor the martyrs we must defend democracy, pursue education and social justice, and work actively in civic life so the sacrifices of 1971 lead to lasting peace and progress for Bangladesh.

Explanation:
The solution breaks the composition into four succinct parts to meet the requested word ranges and to cover meaning, history, observance, and lessons. Part (a) gives a short, clear introduction with date and significance. Part (b) focuses on verified historical milestones: Operation Searchlight (25–26 March), the declaration of independence by Bangabandhu, the nine-month Liberation War, and the surrender on 16 December 1971. Part (c) lists common, verifiable forms of commemoration (flag-hoisting, wreath-laying, cultural programs, media features, memorial visits) to illustrate public practice. Part (d) draws actionable lessons—unity, democracy, education and civic engagement—linking remembrance to present-day responsibilities. The tone is formal and respectful, suitable for a school composition, and the information is organized so each sub-answer can stand alone while together forming a cohesive ~200-word piece.

Question #221 (ID: 578626)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Schools and colleges are reopening after prolonged COVID-19 disruptions. Educators, parents, and policymakers are discussing how classroom teaching should evolve permanently. Consider the pedagogical, technological, equity, and wellbeing aspects when responding to the tasks below.

Options:
a. Write a 200-word composition on "Long-term Effects of COVID-19 on Classroom Teaching."
b. List five key advantages of hybrid (online + in-person) learning that emerged during the pandemic, each with a short explanation.
c. Propose three specific actions governments or school authorities should take to reduce the digital divide revealed by the pandemic. Explain why each action helps.
d. Suggest four practical measures schools can implement to support students' mental health in the post-pandemic period, with a brief implementation note for each.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a The COVID-19 pandemic acted as a catalyst for lasting change in classroom teaching. Schools shifted from rigid, time-bound lessons to flexible, blended approaches that combine face-to-face interactions with digital resources. Teachers adopted a wider range of instructional strategies—synchronous video lessons, flipped-classroom models, and asynchronous modules—allowing learning to be personalized and paced to student needs. Assessment evolved beyond high-stakes exams toward continuous, formative feedback using digital tools. Professional development became integral as educators learned to design online activities, use learning management systems, and analyze student data. Equity challenges exposed during lockdowns pushed institutions to prioritize access: device lending, offline learning packets, and community Wi-Fi hubs became common. Social-emotional learning gained prominence, with schools integrating mental health check-ins and wellbeing curricula to address isolation and anxiety. Classroom spaces were rethought to support collaborative, project-based work rather than solely teacher-led lectures. While disparities remain, the net effect is a more resilient, adaptable educational model—one that values technology as an enabler, emphasizes teacher training, and centers students’ holistic needs for a post-pandemic future.

b 1) Flexibility: Students can access lessons anytime, accommodating varied schedules and learning paces.
2) Personalization: Digital tools enable tailored content and adaptive practice based on individual performance.
3) Resource richness: Online platforms provide multimedia resources, simulations, and global materials beyond textbooks.
4) Continuity of learning: When disruptions occur (illness, weather), hybrid models maintain instructional flow.
5) Increased engagement: Interactive online activities and in-class collaborative tasks together diversify learning experiences.

c 1) Public investment in devices: Governments should fund device-provision programs (loaner laptops/tablets) so all students can access online learning; this removes the primary hardware barrier.
2) Expand affordable broadband: Subsidize community Wi-Fi, partner with ISPs for low-cost home internet, and install connectivity in schools and libraries to ensure reliable access.
3) Local digital hubs and training: Create school or community tech centers and run digital-literacy workshops for students, parents, and teachers so devices and connectivity translate into effective learning.

d 1) Regular wellbeing check-ins: Short weekly surveys or homeroom check-ins identify students needing support; train staff to respond and refer.
2) On-site counseling and referral pathways: Increase school counselor availability and clear links to external mental-health services for timely care.
3) Social-emotional learning (SEL) curriculum: Integrate SEL lessons (coping, empathy, time management) into timetables to build resilience.
4) Safe social reconnection activities: Organize small-group projects, clubs, and supervised play that rebuild peer relationships and reduce isolation.

Explanation:
The composition (a) synthesizes observed shifts during the pandemic: adoption of blended pedagogy, assessment changes, emphasis on teacher training, and increased focus on wellbeing. For (b), advantages chosen reflect core strengths of hybrid models—flexibility, personalization, richer resources, resilience to disruptions, and varied engagement strategies—each supported by widespread experience in remote/hybrid instruction. The actions in (c) tackle access at three levels: devices, connectivity, and capability; all are necessary because having only one without the others leaves students excluded. For (d), mental-health measures combine early detection (check-ins), professional support (counseling), preventive education (SEL), and rebuilding social ties; together they form a continuum from prevention to intervention. These responses are practical, scalable, and informed by lessons from schools worldwide during COVID-19, aiming to make post-pandemic education more equitable, flexible, and supportive of learners’ academic and emotional needs.

Question:

b. List five practical actions the government can take in the next five years to strengthen women's education.
c. Provide two short, original sentences (one encouraging and one cautionary) that could serve as pull-quotes in the magazine.

Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Education is the most powerful tool for transforming lives, and in Bangladesh it has become central to women’s empowerment. In recent decades, the country has seen remarkable gains: girls’ enrollment in primary and secondary schools has risen, female literacy has improved, and more women are graduating from universities and entering the workforce. Education broadens aspirations, builds confidence, and equips women with skills to participate in economic, social, and political life. Yet obstacles remain. Poverty, early marriage, social barriers, insufficient school infrastructure, and safety concerns still force many girls out of classrooms. To overcome these challenges, communities, parents, and policymakers must act together. Investment in safe school facilities, scholarship programs for disadvantaged girls, targeted vocational training, and campaigns to change social attitudes are essential. Female teacher recruitment and gender-sensitive curricula help create welcoming learning environments. Legal enforcement against child marriage and support services for adolescent mothers will also keep girls connected to education. When girls learn, families and communities benefit: healthier children, higher household incomes, and stronger civic participation follow. Explanation:
The composition (a) summarizes the theme by combining positive progress with existing barriers and practical solutions, following the requested structure (introduction, current status, barriers, solutions, conclusion). The five government actions (b) are chosen for feasibility and impact: financial incentives increase attendance; improved facilities and transportation address safety and hygiene; female teachers provide role models and safer learning environments; legal enforcement and re-entry policies protect vulnerable girls; vocational/STEM programs link learning to livelihoods. The two pull-quotes (c) are concise and suitable for a magazine layout—one motivating, one warning—to create emotional balance. The three indicators (d) were selected to cover access (enrollment), learning pathway outcomes (completion and transitions), and real-world impact (employment and earnings). Together these metrics provide a balanced monitoring framework: inputs/outcomes (enrollment/completion) and long-term impact (economic participation), enabling policymakers to target interventions and measure whether education delivers empowerment in practice.

I hope you are well. I am writing to invite you to an educational one-day trip to the Springfield Botanical Garden organized by our class on Saturday, April 12. We will meet at the school gate at 7:30 a.m. sharp and travel by school bus. Please bring a water bottle, a packed lunch, a hat, sunscreen, and a small notebook for observations. The contribution for transport and entry is $8 per student; please bring the money to school this Friday.

We plan to return to school by 5:00 p.m. Please let me know by Friday morning if you can come so I can include you in the final list.

Hope you will join us for a fun and informative day.

Yours sincerely,

Arif
Class 9B

b
Dear Maya, Come with us to the Botanical Garden on Saturday, April 12. Meet at school gate 7:30 a.m. Bring a packed lunch and $8. Please tell me by Friday. — Arif

c
Hi Maya! School trip to the Botanical Garden on Sat, Apr 12. Meet 7:30am at school gate. Bring lunch, water, hat + $8. Can you join? Reply asap.

d
Benefits:
1) Hands-on learning: See and identify plants discussed in class, which helps remember botanical concepts better.
2) Relaxation & inspiration: Spending time outdoors reduces stress and sparks curiosity and creativity.
3) Social bonding: A chance to get to know classmates and strengthen friendships outside the classroom.

Timetable (brief):
- 7:30 a.m. — Meet at school gate and depart by bus
- 9:00 a.m. — Arrive at the Botanical Garden; guided tour and plant study
- 12:30 p.m. — Lunch and free exploration (sketching/photography/notes)
- 3:00 p.m. — Group activities and quiz; prepare to return
- 5:00 p.m. — Arrive back at school


Explanation:
The letter (a) is formal in tone because it serves as an invitation that includes essential logistical details: date, meeting place/time, items to bring, cost, and return time. Including a deadline for confirmation helps organizers finalize numbers. The postcard (b) is concise but retains critical information for quick reading. The WhatsApp message (c) is short and casual, suitable for instant confirmation; it highlights the essentials. The benefits (d) emphasize educational, emotional, and social advantages to motivate participation. The timetable breaks the day into clear slots so the invitee understands the flow of the trip and can plan accordingly.

Question:
Suppose you are Mira / Miraj. You want to invite your nephew Sam who lives in the city to spend the winter holidays with you at your village cottage by the river. Prepare a set of materials related to this invitation: the invitation letter, postal address/stamp layout, a short list of planned activities, and a sample reply from Sam accepting the invitation.

Options:
a. Write the invitation letter to Sam (include date, greeting, body, and closing).
b. Write the postal address block (From / To) and show where the stamp should go.
c. List three specific activities you will organize during the holidays and briefly describe each.
d. Write a short sample reply from Sam accepting the invitation.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a
Greenfield Cottage
Riverside Lane, Oakvale
18 December 2025

Dear Sam,

How are you? I hope you are keeping well and doing fine at school. I am writing to invite you to spend the upcoming winter holidays with me at our cottage in Oakvale. The weather here will be crisp and clear — perfect for fireside stories and long walks by the river.

We plan to welcome you on Friday, 26 December. There will be a warm room ready for you, and I will arrange for your travel from the city station. During your stay we will have a cosy campfire, go for short hikes, visit the nearby farmer's market, and try our hand at fishing by the river. I know how much you enjoy exploring, so I am sure you will have a good time.

Please let me know if 26 December works for you and whether you need any special arrangements for travel or food. I am looking forward to spending time with you and making some wonderful holiday memories.

With love,

Mira

b

From:
Mira
Greenfield Cottage
Riverside Lane
Oakvale 37009

To:
Sam Johnson
Flat 4B, Maple Apartments
78 Central Avenue
Cityville 12005

(Place the postage stamp in the top right corner of the envelope above the 'To' address.)

c
1) Campfire Story Night — An evening by the river with a small, safe campfire, hot chocolate, and family stories. Guests will be encouraged to bring one short story or memory to share.

2) Riverbank Nature Walk & Sketching — A guided morning walk to identify birds and plants, followed by a short sketching session where Sam can draw scenes from nature.

d
12 December 2025

Dear Aunt Mira,

Thank you so much for your invitation. I would love to come and spend the winter holidays at Greenfield Cottage. 26 December is perfect for me. I am really excited about the campfire and the river walks — and I would love to help with the cooking session.

Could you please tell me what time I should arrive at the city station and whether you will pick me up? Also, I have no special dietary needs. I will bring a small notebook for sketches and a warm sweater.

See you soon!

Lots of love,
Sam

Explanation:
This solution provides all requested materials. The postal block (b) shows the From and To addresses and indicates where to place the stamp so the envelope is correctly prepared for mailing. The three activities (c) are concrete, varied (evening, morning, daytime), and age-appropriate; each includes a brief description so Sam knows what to expect. The sample reply (d) is short, courteous, and confirms the proposed date while asking a practical question about pickup time — demonstrating how the invited person would accept and clarify logistics. The overall structure models clear, polite family correspondence and logistical planning for a short holiday visit.

Question #228 (ID: 578620)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You have been asked to prepare a short composition (about 200 words) for a school magazine on 'Plastic Pollution and Its Consequences.' The composition should cover an introduction, main causes, environmental and human impacts, and possible remedies. Additionally, provide a single introductory sentence, list three primary causes, and list three practical solutions that individuals and communities can adopt.

Options:
a. Write the full composition in about 200 words.
b. Give a single clear introductory sentence for the composition.
c. List three primary causes of plastic pollution (brief).
d. List three practical solutions individuals or communities can adopt (brief).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Composition — Plastic Pollution and Its Consequences:

Plastic pollution has become one of the most urgent environmental challenges of our time, spreading from city streets into oceans and remote natural habitats. Single-use plastics, improper waste management, and a throwaway consumer culture have led to vast quantities of plastic debris accumulating in landfills, rivers, and seas. Marine animals ingest or become entangled in plastic, disrupting food chains and causing deaths, while microplastics infiltrate water, soil, and even the air we breathe, posing potential health risks to humans. Plastic production also relies on fossil fuels, contributing to greenhouse gas emissions and climate change. Low-income communities often suffer the most from inadequate waste services, facing polluted environments and associated diseases. To combat this crisis, we must reduce plastic consumption by choosing reusable products, improving recycling and collection systems, and supporting legislation that limits single-use plastics and encourages producer responsibility. Community clean-up drives, education campaigns, and innovations in biodegradable materials can further mitigate impacts. Protecting ecosystems and public health requires combined action from individuals, industries, and governments; only through coordinated effort can we curb plastic pollution and preserve a healthier planet for future generations.

b Introductory sentence:
Plastic pollution, driven by excessive single-use plastics and poor waste management, threatens ecosystems, wildlife, and human health across the globe.

c Three primary causes (brief):
1. Excessive production and use of single-use plastic items (bags, bottles, packaging).
2. Inadequate waste collection, disposal, and recycling infrastructure.
3. Littering and lack of public awareness leading to plastics entering natural environments.

d Three practical solutions (brief):
1. Adopt reusable alternatives (cloth bags, refillable bottles) and refuse single-use plastics.
2. Improve waste management and recycling systems; implement producer responsibility laws.
3. Organize community clean-ups and education programs to reduce litter and change consumer habits.

Explanation:
This solution provides a concise 200-word style composition covering introduction, causes, effects, and remedies for plastic pollution. The introductory sentence (b) is a focused summary to lead the composition. The three causes (c) highlight production/consumption patterns, infrastructure gaps, and behavioral factors—these are commonly identified drivers in environmental studies and policy reports. The three solutions (d) combine individual actions (reuse), systemic policies (improved waste systems and producer responsibility), and community-level efforts (clean-ups and education), reflecting a multi-level approach required to address plastic pollution effectively. The composition emphasizes ecological impacts (entanglement, ingestion, microplastics), human health concerns, and links to fossil-fuel based production to show the broader environmental context. The recommended remedies target both demand reduction and improved management, which are standard best-practice responses in environmental management literature.

Question #229 (ID: 578617)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: Prepare a short composition entitled "Child Marriage: Social Consequences and Community Solutions". Use the context below to answer the sub-questions.

Options:
a. Write a brief introduction (about 40–50 words) defining child marriage and its prevalence.
b. List five primary causes of child marriage (short phrases or single sentences).
c. Describe three major negative consequences of child marriage (each in one or two sentences).
d. Propose four practical community-level solutions to prevent child marriage (each as a clear action point).


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Child marriage is the union of a girl or boy before they reach the legal adult age, often before 18. It remains common in many low-income and traditional communities where poverty, gender norms, and lack of schooling push families to marry children early. Such marriages violate rights and limit life opportunities.

b 1) Poverty—families marry children to reduce economic burden.
2) Lack of education—when schooling is scarce, marriage seems inevitable.
3) Gender norms and family honor—pressure to preserve perceived reputation.
4) Early pregnancy fears and premarital relationship stigma—parents marry daughters to avoid perceived risk.
5) Weak law enforcement and traditional practices—laws exist but are poorly implemented.

c 1) Interrupted education—young brides typically drop out of school, limiting future employment and independence.
2) Health risks—early pregnancy increases maternal and newborn complications and mortality.
3) Psychological and social harm—young spouses face isolation, domestic violence, and long-term poverty, perpetuating intergenerational disadvantage.

d 1) Keep girls in school—scholarships, safe transport, and flexible programs to increase retention.
2) Community awareness campaigns—engage parents, elders, and religious leaders to change norms.
3) Strengthen and enforce laws—train local officials, register marriages, and penalize violators.
4) Economic support for families—cash transfers, skills training, and incentives to reduce the financial drive to marry children.

Explanation:
The introduction (a) sets a concise definition and frames prevalence and consequences to orient readers. The causes (b) are common, evidence-based drivers found in studies: poverty, limited education, social norms, fear of premarital sex, and weak enforcement often interact to produce child marriage. The consequences (c) focus on education, health, and psychosocial outcomes—each supported by global research showing higher maternal mortality, reduced schooling, and increased domestic violence among child brides. The solutions (d) are practical, community-level interventions: education reduces demand for early marriage; awareness shifts cultural norms; legal enforcement raises the cost of arranging child marriages; economic supports remove immediate financial incentives. Combining these measures is most effective because causes are interconnected: addressing only one factor usually has limited impact. Monitoring, community participation, and survivor-centered services (health, counseling) further strengthen prevention and recovery efforts.

Question #230 (ID: 578615)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Context: You are preparing materials for a class on urban livelihoods and have been asked to create content about a street vendor. The content will be used to teach empathy and awareness about informal workers. Use the prompt below to develop several pieces: a full short composition, a concise introduction paragraph, a list of common problems faced by the worker, and practical measures to improve their lives.

Options:
a. Write a short composition (about 200 words) titled "A Street Vendor's Day".
b. Write an introductory paragraph (40-50 words) that hooks the reader and sets the tone for the composition.
c. List five common struggles a street vendor faces, each with a one-line explanation.
d. Suggest three practical measures (with one-sentence justification each) that society or government can take to improve street vendors' lives.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a A Street Vendor's Day

Before sunrise, Rizwan lifts his worn stall-cart and arranges his small display of fruit, snacks, and bottled water. He chooses a corner near a busy bus stop, mindful of the morning crowd. For hours he balances quick sales with polite smiles, calling out prices, weighing fruit, and packaging small orders. Rain or shine, he remains on the pavement: wary of shopkeepers, city officials, and the occasional police sweep that could force him to relocate. Midday is a short respite when he eats a simple meal and counts the day’s earnings—often barely enough to cover rent and supplies. Children sometimes hover, helping in exchange for lessons or change. As evening approaches, Rizwan sells the last pieces, folds his makeshift awning, and walks home tired but hopeful for tomorrow. Though his earnings are low and unpredictable, his service is vital: commuters, office workers, and students depend on his convenience and affordability. Despite the dignity of his labor, Rizwan dreams of stability—legal recognition, safer storage for goods, and access to affordable healthcare. Until then, he carries on with resilience and quiet pride, a single resilient thread in the city's vibrant tapestry.

b Introduction (45 words)

At the break of dawn, a street vendor sets up on a familiar corner where the city breathes fastest. With a small cart and larger hopes, they trade convenience and cheer for uncertain earnings—serving the daily rush while navigating obstacles that most passersby never see.

c Five common struggles

1. Income instability — Daily earnings fluctuate, making budgeting and saving difficult.
2. Lack of legal recognition — No official permit or rights exposes vendors to eviction and fines.
3. Poor working conditions — Long hours outdoors without shelter, sanitation, or storage.
4. Limited access to services — Difficulty obtaining healthcare, banking, or social protection.
5. Social stigma and harassment — Vendors often face discrimination, confiscation of goods, or pressure from authorities.

d Three practical measures

1. Issue affordable street-vending licenses — Legal recognition reduces evictions and allows regulation that protects both vendors and public order.
2. Create designated vending zones with basic facilities — Providing water, waste bins, and covered stalls improves hygiene and working conditions.
3. Offer microcredit and social insurance schemes — Small loans and basic health or income protection help vendors invest in their business and cope with shocks.

Explanation:
This task breaks the topic into four complementary parts: a full composition to give an empathetic narrative, a concise intro to teach how to hook readers, a factual list to identify recurring hardships, and practical measures that are realistic and policy-oriented. The 200-word composition paints a day-in-the-life portrait to humanize the vendor and highlight systemic issues. The 45-word introduction demonstrates economy of language while setting tone. The five struggles capture economic, legal, health, and social dimensions common to informal workers. The three suggested measures are chosen for feasibility and impact: legal recognition addresses root vulnerability, designated zones tackle immediate working conditions, and financial/social tools increase resilience. These components can be used in class discussions, empathy exercises, or as prompts for civic engagement projects.

Question #231 (ID: 578616)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
You are asked to compose a short piece (about 200 words) on the topic "Corruption and Its Impact on Public Services". Use the composition to illustrate causes, consequences, and remedies, and then answer the follow-up items.

Options:
a. Write the requested composition (about 200 words) on "Corruption and Its Impact on Public Services."
b. List three main causes of corruption that particularly harm public services, briefly explaining each.
c. Suggest four practical measures that government and citizens can take to reduce corruption in public services, with a short justification for each measure.
d. Write a one-sentence concluding remark that emphasizes why fighting corruption in public services matters.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Corruption and Its Impact on Public Services

Corruption undermines the very foundations of public services by diverting resources, eroding trust, and diminishing quality. When funds intended for schools, hospitals, roads, and sanitation are siphoned off through bribery, embezzlement, or patronage, infrastructure decays and essential services fail to reach those who need them most. Teachers and health workers may be hired through nepotism rather than merit, reducing service effectiveness. Bribes delay or distort access to care, permits, and utilities, creating inequality where the wealthy receive faster, better service while the poor are left behind. Corruption also inflates costs, deters investment, and weakens institutions that should protect public welfare. Long-term effects include lower educational outcomes, poorer public health, and stunted economic growth. Restoring integrity requires transparency in budgets and procurement, strong independent oversight, digitization of services to reduce discretionary contact, protection for whistleblowers, and civic engagement to hold officials accountable. When public services operate transparently and fairly, resources reach their intended purposes, citizens regain trust, and social development advances. Tackling corruption is therefore essential not only for efficient service delivery but for social justice and sustainable progress.

b Three main causes:
1) Weak accountability systems — Lack of independent audits and enforceable sanctions lets officials act with impunity. 
2) Low public-sector wages and poor working conditions — Financial pressure and low morale increase vulnerability to bribery. 
3) Excessive discretion and opaque procedures — When rules are unclear or hidden, opportunities for favoritism and kickbacks multiply.

c Four practical measures:
1) Transparent e-procurement and budgeting — Reduces human discretion and makes spending traceable. 
2) Strong oversight institutions and independent auditors — Detect and deter misuse of funds. 
3) Whistleblower protection and public reporting channels — Encourage reporting of abuses without fear of retaliation. 
4) Civic education and participatory monitoring — Empowers citizens to demand service standards and exposes local corruption.

d Concluding remark:
Fighting corruption in public services is vital to ensure fairness, restore public trust, and enable sustainable development for all.

Explanation:
The composition (part a) defines corruption and links it directly to concrete harms in public services (education, health, infrastructure), then outlines remedies—this structure mirrors common essay expectations and addresses causes, effects, and solutions. Part b isolates three systemic causes that commonly enable corruption: weak accountability, low pay, and discretionary/opaque processes; each cause is chosen because it is both common and actionable. Part c offers practical, evidence-based measures: digitization (e-procurement/budgeting) reduces face-to-face opportunities for bribery; independent oversight increases detection and punishment; whistleblower protections create safe channels for reporting; and civic participation increases monitoring and social pressure. Each measure is briefly justified to show how it counters specific causes. The one-sentence conclusion (part d) reinforces the moral and practical stakes. The answers aim to be concise yet specific so they can be used directly as components in a short essay or as policy-oriented talking points.

Question #232 (ID: 578606)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Compose a short essay about "Social Media and Responsible Use" suitable for school students. The essay should be clear, balanced, and roughly 200 words in total. Use simple language and include positive and negative aspects as well as practical tips for safe use.

Options:
a. Give a concise, engaging title for the essay.
b. Write an introduction of about 40–60 words that sets the scene and states the main idea.
c. List four benefits of social media and explain each benefit in one sentence.
d. Write a conclusion of about 40–60 words that summarizes the message and gives two practical tips for responsible use.


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a Title: Social Media and Responsible Use
b Introduction: Social media has become a central part of daily life, connecting people across distances and providing fast access to news, learning, and creativity. While it opens many doors for communication and opportunity, young users must learn to use it wisely to avoid distraction, misinformation, and privacy risks. Responsible habits help make social media a positive force for growth and community.
c Benefits: 1) Connectivity: Social media lets friends and family stay in touch despite physical distance, strengthening relationships. 2) Learning: Educational content, tutorials, and discussion groups give students access to diverse knowledge and study help. 3) Voice and Creativity: Platforms allow young people to share art, opinions, and projects, fostering creativity and confidence. 4) Opportunity: Networking and self-promotion on social media can lead to internships, collaborations, and career exposure.
d Conclusion and Tips: Social media can support learning, creativity, and social bonds when used with care; however, users should be aware of its potential harms like distraction, false information, and privacy loss. Tip 1: Verify information from multiple reliable sources before sharing. Tip 2: Set daily time limits, use privacy settings, and talk with trusted adults about any troubling interactions.

Explanation:
The solution is structured to mirror a short school essay while answering each sub-question explicitly. The title (a) is concise and signals the essay's focus. The introduction (b) uses 40–60 words to define the topic and present the balanced stance: benefits exist, but caution is needed. The four benefits (c) are each stated in one clear sentence to meet the requirement and cover social, educational, creative, and practical advantages. The conclusion (d) summarizes the dual nature of social media and gives two concrete, age-appropriate tips: verify information and manage time/privacy. These elements teach composition structure—title, introduction, body points, and conclusion—and provide actionable guidance for responsible use. Word choices are simple and suitable for school students; tone is informative and encouraging rather than alarmist.
